Anglo-American-Japanese Naval Negotiations Reach a Moment of Grave Crisis 18

Japan Proposes a Gradual Approach to Equality

Britain and the US Insist on the Current Ratio System

Roosevelt Suddenly Has Lengthy Talk with Stimson

London: The naval talks between the UK, the US, and Japan have reached a critical stage. It is hoped that today's meeting between the US and Japanese representatives may break the deadlock and provide a turning point toward a compromise. The US and Japanese representatives are now well aware of each other's views and are planning to communicate in order to find a basis for future discussions. Japan's position is currently very difficult to grasp. Although Japan does not want to equalize its navy with other countries immediately, it hopes to achieve this within a few years if the UK and the US allow it to have equal naval rights. However, both the UK and the US have expressed their firm determination to maintain the 5:5:3 ratio. Therefore, they will likely oppose the gradual approach to equality because it is equivalent to breaking the ratio. The current situation can be described as a moment of grave crisis. (Reuters dispatch, 31st)

Washington: President Roosevelt met with former Secretary of State Stimson of the Hoover administration for a long time today. According to Stimson, the discussion was about ordinary diplomatic matters. However, at a time when the London naval talks are underway, special attention should be paid to the inside story of US-Japanese relations. H.H. Bell, Director of the Far Eastern Division of the State Department, and other officials from the State Department's financial department were also summoned after the President met with Stimson. They had recently been involved in commercial and tax negotiations. (National Telegraph, 30th)

Saito Arrives in America to Explain Demand for Equality 19

Can Stipulate Completion in Several Years

But Unwilling to Accept Equality on Paper

Washington: Japanese Ambassador to the United States, Saito, told the press today that Japan does not seek naval equality with the UK and the US, but only wishes to achieve this goal within a few years. Ambassador Saito recently returned to Japan to consult with leaders of the Foreign Ministry and the Navy. His remarks after returning to his post are likely to ease the tense atmosphere caused by Japan's demands at the London naval talks. According to reports from London, Japan is demanding immediate equality. Although Ambassador Saito has made this explanation, he also stated firmly that the equality that Japan is referring to is the equality of warship tonnage, not empty talk of equality in name only. Some have interpreted this statement as a response to the US proposal published in the newspapers, namely that the strength of warships should be based on the relative security of each country. According to this proposal, Japan, due to its isolated geographic position, has a 35% special security advantage. Therefore, if it has 65% of the naval strength, it is already equal to the UK and the US. Ambassador Saito said that Japan will only be satisfied if the number of warships and gun positions is equal. If other countries are willing to reduce their numbers, Japan is also willing to reduce its numbers, as long as it can achieve equality in the end. Saito denied that the Japanese government is currently planning to sign a non-aggression treaty with the United States. As for yesterday's news that the US Navy has completed plans to build defenses at its Pacific naval and air bases in response to Japan's demand to abolish the naval treaty, Saito did not comment. (National Telegraph, 30th)

US-Japan Hold Third Meeting, Japan Still Explains Principles 20

Explains Offensive and Defensive Armaments

London: The US and Japanese delegations were originally scheduled to meet today, but due to conflicting opinions between the two sides, the meeting was canceled and postponed to another day. US Representative Davis is resting due to fatigue. The Japanese delegation will host the US delegation at the Japanese Embassy on the 31st to explain Japan's interpretation of offensive and defensive weapons. (Japan United Press dispatch, 30th)

London: The Japanese delegation has held two meetings each with the UK and the US to explain Japan's disarmament policy, but has not gained the recognition of the two countries. As a result, the conflict between Japan and the UK and the US will become more profound. Ambassador Matsudaira has therefore decided to conduct negotiations in the form of private talks. He visited British Foreign Secretary Simon on the afternoon of the 30th to exchange views. Matsudaira also met with US Representative Davis on the afternoon of the 31st at 4:30 to exchange views. (Japan United Press dispatch, 30th)

London: Japanese Ambassador Matsudaira visited the British Parliament on the afternoon of the 30th and met with Foreign Secretary Simon in the Foreign Secretary's office for secret talks. (Japan United Press dispatch, 30th)

London: US and Japanese naval representatives are scheduled to hold important talks at 4:30 PM today to make progress on the naval issue. According to those around US Chief Representative Davis, the US representatives plan to further explore the details of the Japanese proposal and begin discussing the figures requested by Japan during today's exchange of views. On the Japanese side, however, it seems determined to first obtain agreement on the major principles put forward by Japan before further discussing the figures. Therefore, the views of both sides are still in conflict. However, this afternoon, a way may be found to mask the fundamental conflict between the two sides, or at least to find a way to keep the negotiations going. When British Foreign Secretary Simon met with Japanese Ambassador to the UK Matsudaira last night, he expressed the British Cabinet's desire to do so. As for the US, it has consistently exercised caution to avoid a breakdown in negotiations, as the US Congress will soon hold local elections, and if the negotiations break down, domestic public opinion in the US will be very unfavorable to the government. However, so far, the fundamental attitudes of all parties toward this issue remain irreconcilable. (Havas dispatch, 31st)

US Farmers Again Target Japanese 24

Bombs Thrown into Japanese Farmers' Homes

Governor Orders Foreign Farmers to Leave

Phoenix, USA: The Governor's Office here received a report today that there were renewed anti-Japanese demonstrations in the Salt River Valley. It is said that unknown persons threw bombs into two Japanese farmers' homes near Glendale this morning. One home suffered heavy losses, so the relationship between the Japanese and local farmers there has become tense again. Two other Japanese farms elsewhere were also attacked with bombs. One exploded, shattering the windows and injuring a Japanese child. It is heard that Arizona Governor Moe is prepared to take measures to prevent such incidents from happening again, but there have been previous bombings and no prevention has been seen. The root cause of the mutual hatred is that the economic levels of Japanese and American farmers are different. American farmers believe that they cannot cope with the competition from the Japanese, so incidents have occurred repeatedly. The governments of both Japan and the US have also had informal discussions, but Japan has repeatedly stated that it believes that local officials can handle the matter properly, so it has not formally protested so far. (National Telegraph, 30th)

(Havas dispatch, 31st)

London: Parliament reconvened today to discuss a wide range of issues, including war debts, unemployment, and shipping. Responding to a question about the issue of wearing party uniforms, Home Secretary Gilmour said that the matter was still under consideration by the Home Office, but he could not state whether the government would submit legislation on the matter to the next Parliament. He could continue to discuss the matter with the leaders of the opposition parties. Financial Secretary to the War Office, Hacking, denied the rumor that the government intended to move the Woolwich Arsenal to another location to prevent aerial attacks, and said that the entire issue was under consideration, but he could not make any comments on the matter at this time. Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain stated that negotiations were not currently underway regarding the British debt to the US, and that he could not make any statement regarding the installment due on December 15th. In short, there was no new development to report. Prime Minister MacDonald stated that the government's special committee to investigate the disaster situation in the unemployed areas had issued a report, and the investigators had agreed on several proposals. In view of the importance of the matter, the government intended to designate a day to discuss the published report in October. The House of Commons asked the government to allow a debate on the private arms trade. The Prime Minister immediately agreed. President of the Board of Trade Runciman stated that on September 28th, shipping companies had submitted a plan to the government to subsidize merchant ships without fixed routes in order to alleviate the difficulties of the shipping industry. Legislation would be necessary to implement this plan. The government had contacted overseas autonomous regions and India and several foreign governments on this matter. It is now heard that the Chamber of Shipping is trying to convene an international shipping conference to develop ways to adjust the supply of tonnage according to demand. (Reuters dispatch, 30th)

London: The government's rigorous Incitement to Disaffection Act is strongly opposed, as can be seen during today's review in the House of Commons. Liberal Party member Marlaud moved to add a new clause stipulating that when the police search a house, they must summon two or more respectable neighbors to supervise the search. The member also said that the Indian Penal Code of 1898 contained a similar clause. The Labour Party in the House of Commons supported the motion, but the Royal Law Advisor General Inskip and the Prosecutor General opposed it, considering it impractical and unnecessary. Inskip said that the clause contained in the Indian Penal Code of 1898 does not force people to be witnesses to police searches of houses, and the situation in India is very different from that in the UK. The motion was defeated by 325 votes to 79. (Reuters dispatch, 30th)

German Church Crisis 31

Hitler Negotiates with the Opposition

Expresses Displeasure at Church Split

Berlin: Thirty representatives of the Bavarian National Socialist Party farmers, who claimed to represent 200,000 Bavarian Christians, reportedly met with German Head of State Hitler today to discuss the German Church crisis. However, an official of the Chancellery denied that Hitler had received these people. It is said that one of Hitler's subordinates met with the delegation, listened to their explanations, and then asked them to go to the Ministry of the Interior. This morning, the farmers lined up to go to the Chancellery. A Black Guard soldier on duty wanted to order them to leave, so the farmers told him in Bavarian, "Mind your own business. They will tell the head of state the truth about the church." Later, the leader of the delegation claimed that after seeing the head of state, they told him that Dr. Müller and Prussian Interior Minister Dr. Goebbels were destroying the Lutheran Church and must be removed from office. This afternoon, Hitler met with Bavarian Bishop Meiser and others, the three leaders who opposed the German National Church, for about two hours, but the results of the talks were not revealed. It is heard that the three bishops are currently discussing the current situation. Their report will be the basis for the upcoming discussions by representatives of the opposition church members on future attitudes. A senior government official told a Reuters interviewer today that Hitler did not want to personally interfere in the church dispute and would hand the matter over to the Ministry of the Interior for proper handling. According to political sources, Hitler is willing to have all factions of the church hold a round table conference to discuss peaceful cooperation. Prussian Interior Minister Dr. Goebbels has resigned from his church position due to pressure from the National Socialist Party. (Reuters dispatch, 30th)

Berlin: The German news agency recently released a message saying that Head of State Hitler received three bishops of Bavaria, Württemberg, and Hanover yesterday. These three are all famous for opposing the national church, and among them, bishops Bavier and Wittenberg have also been dismissed by the church legal management committee Jagel and are no longer bishops. Now Hitler has received them all, and this message is released by the official news agency, which is particularly noteworthy. According to a general investigation, Hitler is very displeased with the internal divisions of the Evangelical Church. When he received the three bishops yesterday, he seemed to have expressed his decision not to support the national church again. Therefore, after this message came out, those who relied on Hitler's protection were very uneasy, while those who were not from the national church felt that Hitler's change of attitude was very fortunate for the future of the German Jesus Church. (Havas dispatch, 31st)

Germany Severely Punishes Traitors 32

Acting as spies for foreign countries to be punished with the utmost penalty

Berlin – According to today's news, the People's Court recently sentenced several people accused of being foreign spies to severe punishments. Several were sentenced to death, and many were sentenced to several years of imprisonment and hard labor. Only two were sentenced to ordinary imprisonment. According to official sources, these punishments were imposed in accordance with the old laws, because the crimes were committed before the promulgation of the new laws. According to the new law, any German who betrays the country will lose his life. Because the National Socialist Party places the welfare of the entire nation first, it does not hesitate to impose the death penalty on traitors and spies. (31st Reuters dispatch)

Train Engine of the Bulgarian King Catches Fire? 37

The King drives for two hours

Rumors of assassination are unreliable

Sofia – Bulgarian King Boris was traveling by express train from Sofia to Varna today when the engine caught fire 140 miles from his destination. The driver was burned by the fire. The King then took care of the injured driver and drove the train himself at full speed to a riverside, where he helped extinguish the fire. He then jumped back into the driver's cab and drove the train safely to Varna, driving for two hours in total. It is said that King Boris liked to drive various machines during the European War, and he often joked that if he lost his throne, he could become a driver to support himself. (30th Reuters dispatch)

Sofia – Foreign newspapers reported that the fire in the engine of the special train of Bulgarian King Boris was caused by a bomb hidden in the coal in the engine. This is hardly credible here. However, it is known that there was no danger in the incident. Because the King's carriage was attached to a passenger train bound for Varna, the engine suddenly caught fire when passing through the Strazhitsa station. The train stopped, and the King immediately rushed to the engine, where he saw that the driver's clothes were on fire. The King pulled down the driver's clothes and moved him to rest on the couch in the King's sleeping car. Although the driver was burned by the fire, his life was not in danger. The King then acted as the driver and drove straight to Varna. As for the rumors of assassinating the King, they are all false. (30th National Telegraph)

Central Political Council Approves Measures for Donating Salaries to Aid Relief 38

Nanjing – The Central Political Council held its 431st regular meeting at 9:00 am on the 31st, attended by Ju Zheng, Ye Chucang, Wang Zhaoming, Sun Ke, Chen Lifu, Chu Minyi, Zhu Peide, Shi Qingyang, Zhu Jiqing, Wang Zhengting, Huang Shaoxiong and other more than 30 people. Sun Ke chaired the meeting and resolved the following important cases: 1. The eight measures for public officials to donate salaries to aid relief were approved and submitted to the National Government for implementation. 2. The request from the Sun Yat-sen County Political Implementation Committee to amend Article 6 of the committee's organizational outline was approved, and Sun Ke was appointed as the chairman of the Sun Yat-sen County Political Implementation Committee. 3. The limitations on spending the second reserve fund and submitting supplementary budget regulations according to the budget regulations were approved. (Regulations attached below) 4. The National Government should instruct all agencies to supplement and submit budget estimates for loan income, construction funds, and operating investment expenditures in accordance with the budget regulations and the regulations on handling budget revenue and expenditure classification standards. 5. Regarding the method of supplementing impeachment cases in the 416th meeting, the following resolutions were made again: 1. After an impeachment case is transferred for disciplinary action, the handling agency should use the impeachment document and the Law on Disciplining Public Officials. 2. For political officials appointed by a resolution of the Central Political Council, when they are subjected to disciplinary action, the decision on their punishment should be reported to the Central Political Council. 3. Regarding the provision that national policies and important documents related to China's international status shall not be disclosed without the approval of the Central Political Council, there were already measures in place in June of this year, and there is no need to repeat the provision.

Measures for Public Officials to Donate Salaries to Aid Relief: 1. All public officials with a monthly salary of 50 yuan or more shall donate 2% of their monthly salary for a total of six months, from November 1934 to April 1935. Those with less than 50 yuan are exempt from donation. 2. Personnel from agencies such as the Salt Administration, Railways, Post Office, and Telecommunications Administration, as well as all state-owned and publicly operated enterprises, shall donate in accordance with the regulations. 3. Personnel from educational administrative agencies shall donate in accordance with the regulations. Personnel from national and public secondary schools and above, as well as academic and cultural institutions, shall donate in accordance with the regulations. 4. Personnel from police agencies shall donate in accordance with the regulations. 5. Military agency and troop personnel whose salaries have already been discounted shall donate as much as they can. 6. The collection of donations shall be handled by the Ministry of Finance, which shall supervise the provincial finance departments and municipal finance bureaus. The collection of donations from personnel of central agencies shall be the responsibility of the Ministry of Finance. The collection of donations from personnel of local agencies shall be the responsibility of the heads of the agencies and accounting personnel of the provincial finance departments and municipal finance bureaus, and shall be remitted to the Ministry of Finance, provincial finance departments, or municipal finance bureaus together with the donation report form before the 15th of the following month. 7. The Ministry of Finance shall prepare a monthly donation report form and submit it to the Executive Yuan for verification. 8. The distribution of donations shall be handled by the Executive Yuan.

Limitations on Spending the Second Reserve Fund: A. Unexpected incidents should be limited to those that occur after the submission of the annual budget estimate. B. New facilities should be limited to those for which there is a definite reason why they cannot be delayed within the current year. C. Procedures: Prepare a plan and draft estimate, and submit it to the Central Political Council for approval before proceeding.

Limitations on Supplementary Budgets: A. Reasons: Limited to those based on laws or contracts. B. Circumstances: Limited to those that are unavoidable within the current year. C. Procedures: Must be handled in accordance with Section 4 of the Budget Regulations. The same principle applies to self-raising sources for revenue and expenditure matching. If the competent agency submitting the request cannot raise its own funds, the government must attach remedial opinions in accordance with Article 23, Paragraph 2 of the Budget Regulations. (31st Central News Agency dispatch)

Nanjing – The Ministry of Finance has allocated 600,000 yuan of the regular subsidy for this year to Fujian for the Yangmi tax, 30,000 yuan to Anhui to compensate for the cancellation of salt trade fees, and 180,000 yuan for the temporary subsidy for Fujian to expand the Liancheng Highway and 360,000 yuan for Henan to build roads and open rivers, which were sent to the Directorate-General of Budgets, Accounting and Statistics for review by the Central Political Council. The council approved a total of 1.19 million yuan, designated to be spent from the second reserve fund. In addition, the Ministry of Finance also approved the allocation of 175,000 yuan for the Fujian Yangmi tax and 30,000 yuan for the expansion of the Liancheng Highway from the 22nd year, to be spent accordingly. The Hubei Provincial Government telegraphed the Ministry of Finance, requesting that the central government provide 300,000 yuan for political expenses, following the precedents of Jiangsu and Zhejiang. The Ministry of Finance is currently considering this. (31st Special Dispatch)

Central Government Holds Memorial Service for Huang Xing 39

President Wang Reports on the Revolutionary Deeds of Martyr Huang

Bronze Statue of Huang in Wuchang Unveiled

Nanjing – The Central Government held a memorial service for the 18th anniversary of Huang Xing's death at 8:00 am on the 31st, attended by Central Committee members Ye Chucang, Wang Zhaoming, Chen Lifu, Chu Minyi, Zhu Peide, Wang Zhengting, Ma Chaojun, Huang Shaoxiong, Zhu Jiqing, Pan Yunchao, Jiao Yitang, Wang Luyi, and representatives from various agencies and all staff members of the Party Headquarters, totaling about 500 people. Ye Chucang chaired the meeting and conducted the ritual. Later, Wang Zhaoming reported on the revolutionary deeds of Martyr Huang, stating briefly: "The revolutionary achievements of Mr. Huang Xing cannot be fully described in a short time. Only the three most prominent points will be briefly mentioned: 1. When the Boshin War of Independence broke out, the revolutionary organization was scattered. The Premier founded the Tongmenghui, and Mr. Huang Xing was the first to assist the Premier and worked the hardest, finally unifying the will of the revolutionaries and uniting them under the organization of our Party, which then developed day by day. 2. The Huanghuagang Uprising was launched despite the fact that our Party comrades knew it would fail, in order to awaken revolutionary sentiment with blood and flesh and to seek credibility at home and abroad. At that time, Mr. Huang Xing was the one who commanded the comrades in Guangzhou and directed everything, resulting in the martyrdom of the Seventy-Two Martyrs. Huang Xing was also wounded and bled. His loyalty and bravery will be remembered forever by future generations. 3. The success of the Wuchang Uprising in 1911 was due to Mr. Huang Xing commanding a small number of revolutionary troops in Hankou and Hanyang, engaging in bloody battles with Qing soldiers, and holding out for a month. Subsequently, Mr. Chen Qimei responded in Shanghai, and Nanjing was recovered, making the revolutionary momentum in the Jiangnan area majestic and leading to success. From these three events, we know that Mr. Huang Xing's loyalty, bravery, and spirit of hard work and sacrifice not only laid the foundation for the revolution and for our Party, but also laid the foundation for the Republic of China. Today, as we commemorate Mr. Huang Xing and recall his life's achievements, we should strive to emulate his loyalty and bravery, and complete his unfinished great cause, in order to fulfill the responsibilities of those who come after him." After Wang finished his speech, the meeting adjourned. (31st Central News Agency dispatch)

Nanjing – The Nanjing Poor Children's Education Institute held a memorial meeting for the 18th anniversary of the death of its founder, Mr. Huang Xing, at 2:00 pm on the 31st, attended by Niu Yongjian, Yao Yuping, Zhang Tong, representatives from various sectors, and teachers and students of the institute, totaling more than 500 people. Various representatives gave speeches, and the atmosphere was extremely solemn. (31st Central News Agency dispatch)

Hankou – The unveiling ceremony of the bronze statue of Huang Xing at the Yellow Crane Tower in Wuchang and the 18th anniversary of Huang's death were held on the 31st. Zhang Xueliang, He Chengjun, and Zhang Qun all attended the meeting and participated in the ceremony, which was solemn. Huang's wife and son, Eugene, returned to Nanjing. (31st Special Dispatch)

Tianjin – Today is the 18th anniversary of the death of Martyr Huang Xing. The Tianjin City Party Headquarters held a memorial meeting in the auditorium at 9:00 am, attended by more than 40 representatives from various sectors. The ceremony ended at 10:00 am. (31st Special Dispatch)

Changsha – The 31st was the memorial day for Huang, Cai, Jiao, and Chen. He Jian and leaders from all walks of life crossed the river to pay their respects. At the same time, the completion ceremony of the memorial pavilion for the fallen soldiers was held, which was extremely solemn. (31st Special Dispatch)

Cotton Yarn Consolidated Tax Issue 40

Talks with a certain director of the Ministry of Finance

Nanjing – Regarding the increase in the consolidated tax on cotton yarn and the refund of the increased import tax on foreign cotton, according to a certain director of the Ministry of Finance, since the Ministry of Finance implemented the consolidated tax, the tax rates on various goods have increased. At that time, the consolidated tax on domestic cotton yarn was not increased, because the government has been trying to ease the difficulties of merchants and reduce tax revenue. However, the cotton mills have not been relieved by the reduction in the consolidated tax. The reasons for their economic downturn can be divided into three points: 1. The machinery is too old. 2. The management is not scientific. For example, foreign cotton mills can manage more than 30 machines per person, while Chinese merchants can only manage a few machines. Foreign cotton mills have ample capital, while banks charge higher interest rates on loans to Chinese cotton mills. There are many other reasons, but only the major ones are mentioned here. For these reasons, the government believes that it has an unshirkable responsibility to rescue the cotton industry. However, it is certain that rescuing the cotton industry cannot be achieved by reducing the consolidated tax. We should earnestly work from the fundamental aspects. On the one hand, the government will increase the consolidated tax on cotton yarn to balance the tax rates. On the other hand, it should further plan fundamental relief. As for the issue of refunding the increased tax on foreign cotton, domestic cotton used to be American cotton. Now, domestic cotton, such as Shaanxi cotton, etc., uses American cotton seeds. After improvement, the yield and quality have improved. If domestic cotton can be sold as much as possible, the government should protect it. Therefore, the import tax on foreign cotton, which used to be 3.5 gold units per 100 kilograms, has been increased to 5 gold units, an increase of 1.5 yuan. Because the sales of Chinese cotton are becoming more and more widespread, the Ministry of Finance plans to grant a tax refund of 1.5 gold units for the export of foreign cotton in order to promote the sale of domestic cotton to foreign markets. This measure directly promotes the spread of domestic cotton in the international market and indirectly protects the stability of domestic cotton prices, which is beneficial to Chinese cotton production and diplomacy. In short, foreign merchants now feel that the increase in the consolidated tax on cotton yarn is a sovereign right of the Chinese government, so they respect this reasonable tax increase. Chinese merchants, based on one-sided feelings, have not considered the reasons behind this and hastily petitioned for exemption from the increase, which seems to be somewhat regrettable in terms of national consciousness. (31st Special Dispatch)

Old Stamps to be Completely Abolished from Today 42

Measures for exchanging them have not yet been drafted

Nanjing – The Ministry of Finance's new Pagoda stamps, printed by the Beiping Printing Bureau, have been completed and distributed to post offices in various places, and will be available for purchase on the first day. There are five types: 1 cent, 2 cents, 1 jiao, 5 jiao, and 1 yuan. The 1-cent stamp is brown, the 2-cent stamp is green, the 1-jiao stamp is yellow, the 5-jiao stamp is purple, and the 1-yuan stamp is blue. According to the person in charge of the Taxation Department, old stamps will be completely abolished from the first day. The measures for exchanging old stamps for new stamps have not yet been drafted. The stamps are sold by post offices on behalf of the Ministry of Finance, one to avoid exclusive sales, and the other to enable merchants and people to affix stamps properly. From November 1st onwards, all documents and certificates signed must be affixed with new stamps, otherwise they will be treated as tax evasion. All stamp tax sub-bureaus in various places must be closed by the end of October. Except for retaining one stamp, alcohol and tobacco tax general bureau in each province, all others will be abolished. The investigation matters will be handled by the general bureau. The unemployed employees of the various sub-bureaus had previously asked the Ministry of Finance to distribute them to post offices in various places to be responsible for selling stamps, but this right belongs to the Ministry of Communications, and this Ministry is not in a position to make any claims. Whether there is a solution has not yet been decided. (31st Special Dispatch)

A section of the track was destroyed and a passenger car derailed

Tianjin – The Ping-Shen through train departed from Shenyang for Beiping on the 30th. At 1:30 am on the 31st, when passing Suizhong, about 15 kilometers from the Jizhang station, one section of a third-class passenger car suddenly derailed and a section of the track was destroyed. International Commercial Telegraph

October 31st Reuters Special Commercial News

Gold and Silver 48

London Gold Price: The London gold market quoted a price of 139 shillings and 7 pence today, down three and a half pence.

London Large Bars: In the London silver market, the spot price today fell to 23 and 3/8 pence, down 1/8, and the futures price fell to 23 and 7/16 pence, down 1/4. Speculators selling is the reason for the decline in silver prices. The US government bought in and the closing price stabilized.

Bombay Large Bars: The Bombay silver market fell today. At 5:30 pm, the spot price was 64 rupees, down 15 annas from yesterday, but the market was stable at the close.

Exchange Rates 49

British-American: The London foreign exchange market fluctuated greatly and the market was calm. The British-American exchange rate opened at $4.99, 0.0625 higher than yesterday's US-British closing exchange rate. The exchange rate was slightly lower in the morning, at $4.98 at 1:00 pm, but recovered half a cent at 2:00 pm, to $4.985, half a cent lower than the opening price.

British-French: Fluctuations were narrow and the market was quiet. The opening price was 75.75 francs, 10 pounds higher than yesterday's closing price. It fell 0.16 pounds at 1:00 pm, but recovered 0.06 pounds at 2:00 pm, to 75.65 francs, 0.10 pounds lower than this morning's opening price.

American-British: In the New York foreign exchange market, the American-British exchange rate opened this morning at $4.9875, 0.01875 higher. This price was quite stable, and only fell half a cent at the time of the telegram, to $4.9825.

Cotton and Wheat 50

American Cotton: The New York cotton market opened today, and there were still many purchases by traders. Speculators were not very active. Although the opening price fell 0.03 pounds, it recovered slightly in the morning.

Indian Cotton: The price in the Bombay cotton market also fell today, because European and Japanese merchants were selling. At 5:30 pm, the price of white Luo cotton for the April-May period was 209 rupees and 11 annas, half a rupee lower than yesterday's price.

British Cotton: There was almost no change in the Liverpool market this morning. At 1:00 pm, the price for the January period fell 0.01 pounds, to 6.61.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market was weak in futures trading today because the Argentine wheat market was sluggish. At 1:00 pm, the price for the December period was 4 shillings and 11 pence, half a pence lower than yesterday's closing price.

American Wheat: Although the Chicago wheat market was generally quiet, prices did not change much, but there was an unsettling atmosphere. The weakness of the Winnipeg wheat market was due to the government's management policy, which has not yet improved, and the low price of Argentine wheat were all unsettling factors in the Chicago wheat market. The opening price wanted to rise, but fell shortly after. The recent price is about 1 cent lower than the opening price.

Rubber 51

London: This morning, the London rubber market was affected by yesterday's adjournment of the International Rubber Committee, and prices were therefore uncertain. At noon, the transaction price for the January-March period was 6.5 pence, 0.025 lower than yesterday's closing price.

New York: New York rubber futures prices fell sharply this morning, losing sympathy with the London rubber market. When the International Rubber Committee met yesterday, it failed to reach any agreement on the export quota for next year. This is the reason for the weakness of the British and American rubber markets. The New York opening price fell 0.40 pounds, and there was little recovery in the morning.

Contents of the Regulations for the Custody Committee of Disaster Relief Reserve Funds 58

Nanjing. The Disaster Relief Reserve Fund Law was promulgated by the National Government in October of the 19th year. Recently, the Executive Yuan ordered the Ministry of Interior, in conjunction with the Political Affairs Committee, to draft regulations for the Committee for the Custody of Disaster Relief Reserve Funds and send them to the Ministry of Finance for comments. They will be submitted to the Executive Yuan for review and then promulgated. The main points of the organizational regulations are: the National Government will appoint seven members to form the committee, with the Minister of Interior and the Minister of Finance as ex officio members. The committee will be supervised by the Executive Yuan. The committee's economic expenditures must not use the disaster relief reserve fund. One percent of the total amount of the government's regular budget revenue will be used as the reserve fund, with a maximum amount of 50 million yuan. The reserve fund will be deposited in national banks or reputable banks and will accrue interest on a regular basis. If the disaster relief reserve fund suffers losses due to the negligence of the custodian, the custodian shall be liable for compensation. This year's disaster relief will be paid for with the interest generated by this year's reserve fund. If it is not enough, the reserve fund may be used, but in no case shall it exceed one-half of this year's income. The custody committee shall prepare an annual budget and final accounts and submit them to the supervisory agency. (Special dispatch from the 31st)

Personal Account of the Xinjiang Incident (Part 2) 83

— Kashgar Correspondence.

After the rebel party occupied Hotan, they flocked down, numbering about ten thousand, approaching Pishan. Wang, the company commander of the county's defense forces, immediately led a unit of more than a hundred men (a mixture of Xibe from Yili and Han Chinese) to block them. That night, they marched to Piyaman (the border between Moyu and Pishan) and encountered the rebel party. Because it was dark, they could not ascertain how many there were, so they opened fire indiscriminately. It is estimated that with each bullet fired, at least two or three people were killed (the rebel returnees had no guns, only big-headed clubs). In a short time, about five or six hundred were killed, but in the end, they could not be repelled due to their superior numbers. Near dawn, Company Commander Wang retreated to Pishan (three or four men were killed in action) and immediately sent a letter to Kashgar requesting reinforcements. At this time, it was just after Jin Shuren's death, and Kashgar was in chaos and could not spare any attention. It was not until the end of March (the uprisings in Hotan and Moyu occurred around February 16th) that reinforcements arrived. Ma Shaowu's intention was to appease rather than suppress, but after seeing that there was no other way, he ordered the reinforcements to depart. However, although the reinforcements arrived, they did not dare to attack because of the rebel party's strength. Before long, Yecheng (Yecheng is between Pishan and Shache) also broke out in riots among the people and bandits, and Zepu responded. Many Han Chinese in the two counties were brutally killed. At this time, the rear of the reinforcements was cut off. Knowing that they could not defend, they detoured and retreated to Shache via a small road, with a journey of nine days. They were repeatedly attacked by villagers along the way, resulting in thirteen incidents of opening fire. Although hundreds of rioters were killed, the reinforcements had exhausted their strength before they could retreat to Shache. After the reinforcements retreated to Shache, they joined forces with the county's defense forces and formed a merchant corps from several hundred Han Chinese merchants who had fled from various places in advance and the local Han Chinese, with military and civilians working together (totaling more than a thousand people) to defend the city and asked Kashgar for reinforcements. Although Kashgar sent some reinforcements, they all carried weapons and defected because they were newly recruited people of the cloth and silk classes. Yierqiang also suddenly changed (the city is connected to Shache). At this time, Shache was surrounded on all sides, and the isolated city had no reinforcements. It is estimated that they were besieged for (four or five) months and killed 3,000 rebels who were besieging the city. The rebels did not dare to approach the city within several miles. However, before the siege of Shache was lifted, the Battle of Bachu broke out again. The treacherous and deceitful rebel returnees' previous peace was not sincere. In reality, they wanted to use the truce as an opportunity to carry out their conspiracy to incite and lure troops in the Kashgar area. Turbaned Temir (who had been promoted to regimental commander) sent people to lure Island Siman, the commander of the Buyi battalion (30 years old, spoke Chinese, originally served as Chen's Buyi civilian affairs officer, imprisoned for breaking the law, this time Ma Shaowu specially released him from prison and appointed him as the commander of the Buyi battalion). Island actually led his troops to betray and turn against them, killing the Han Chinese and Hui military officers in the regiment and gathering the Buyi people under his command at the radio station (20 li away from the Hui city), completely destroying all the equipment of the radio station, leaving only three radio poles. At the same time, the Buyi people in the mountains and rioters in various places also rose up in support, gathering five or six thousand people in a few days (fortunately, most of them had no weapons), disturbing the countryside, searching and robbing guns and horses, and also looting property. However, they would wash empty the houses of our Han Chinese. If there were heavy items that could not be carried, they would destroy them, not allowing even a single blade of grass or tree to remain in the house. Fortunately, people had fled into the city, otherwise they would have all been brutally murdered. At that time, the rioters in Jiashi (a county between Kashgar and Bachu) also gathered to riot. Kashgar was alarmed several times a day, and people were panicking. Although the authorities strongly maintained a calm attitude, the society had reached a state of chaos, and the situation in Bachu was particularly urgent. On a certain day in April, Liu Ding was lured and killed. After Kashgar received the report, they immediately ordered the army to retreat to Kashgar as soon as possible, hoping to fight to the death with the city as their backs. When the telegram arrived in Bachu, the area between Jiutai and Bachu had already been cut off by the rebel army. At that time, Yang Qingming was the acting county magistrate of Bachu. Seeing that the situation was critical, he took all the soldiers, more than a hundred men, and one or two hundred Han Chinese refugees from Bachu and retreated towards Kashgar (Bachu is six stations from Kashgar and four stations from Jiashi). When they retreated to Yingwatay (40 li away from Jiashi County), the rebel army had already tracked them down and opened fire dozens of times (according to reports, this time there were only about ten Hui people and ten guns, with the rest being two or three hundred local rioters, but all of them had no weapons). As a result, Yang Qingming was wounded in the leg, and a dozen soldiers were killed or wounded. The rioters forced the remaining ten or so people to surrender their weapons and transferred them to the Bachu Hui commander Ma Zhancang (32 years old, the leader of the plainclothes team, actually an ignorant desperado). After one unit of the Jiutai Kashgar army (about 500 men) learned that the rear route had been cut off, they retreated to Shache via a small road in Mogaidi County (one big station from Shache and four stations from Bachu). However, they were blocked and attacked by the turbaned people along the way. When they reached the edge of Heigaidi, they were caught up by the rebel army and surrendered all their weapons. They were transferred to Bachu. The main force of the rebel party was stationed in Bachu. Their vanguard, the fresh bandits, Ma bandits (Muslims), and Tie bandits (i.e., turbaned bandits Temir, all rebel regimental commanders), as well as the Buyi army (Muslim battalion commander), were all stationed in Jiashi, with a great momentum of advancing straight into Kashgar. At this time, Kashgar was in dire straits, and Ma Shaowu was helpless. However, because of his religious relationship with them, he still sent a letter to negotiate, requesting cooperation and asking for a peaceful resolution. Originally, the rebel party's goal was to rob and plunder. Moreover, Kashgar was a prosperous area in southern Xinjiang, and they had long coveted it. However, they also wanted to avoid a military conflict with the Kashgar army, so they pretended to accept Ma's (Shaowu) request and secretly ordered the Buyi people to attack Shufu (this was originally led by Temir). At dawn on May 2nd, the Buyi people suddenly attacked the city. Because the turbaned people were internal collaborators, the city was captured within a few hours. At this time, all the Han Chinese property and women and children inside and outside the city were looted by the Buyi turbaned people, and all Han Chinese who escaped or were found were killed. At this time, the lives of the Han Chinese were not even worth as much as a chicken. The most tragic thing was that many of the Han Chinese tombs were dug up. Fortunately, there were still a hundred or so Han Chinese who escaped into the Taoist office during the siege. Because the Taoist office had guards defending it, the rioters could not attack, so they were able to save their lives. However, they were all forced by the Buyi and turbaned people to convert to Islam and had to change into turbaned attire and pray five times a day (i.e., the turbaned people's Namaz). If they encountered troops of the Buyi or turbaned people, they had to recite a section of the Quran. If they could not recite it or could not recite it completely, they would be shot immediately. As a result, deaths were heard every day. Later, because they could not survive, they all fled into the Han city. At this time, the rioters in Jiashi and Bachu also arrived one after another. However, most of the Hui troops were stationed in the Han city, and only Ma Zhancang led some rioters stationed in the Hui city. Other rioters, such as the turbaned Temir, were also stationed in the Hui city. At this time, all the government offices and transportation agencies in the Hui city were occupied by the turbaned Hui people. The Han Chinese houses and temples were all destroyed, and they searched every house for Han Chinese possessions. If they encountered Han Chinese books, they would be destroyed. Commander Ma Zhancang was also under his threat at this time and had to follow his will in everything. Therefore, even the dignified religious leader Ma Shaowu did not hesitate to force him to step down. Later, Temir and Ma Zhancang divided the power, each nominally occupying a city. Ma Zhancang believed that the Han city was purely Han Chinese and could be united to defend against Temir's attacks. We Han Chinese knew that using a tiger for protection was tantamount to suicide, but under his power, there was nothing we could do. It is estimated that the party looted more than a million yuan from the Han Chinese in the Han city, and their inhumane acts of looting were worse than those of the Buyi and turbaned people. However, the great power ultimately fell aside because Ma Shiming, the leader of the Yanjing riots, and Ma Ren, the leader of the Aksu riots (leader of the plainclothes team), were all resolved by the turbaned bandits. At this time, the turbaned bandits were powerful and hated the Han Chinese and Hui people from Central China (wanting to organize a pure Turkic country). Although he claimed to be a commander, he was actually in a position of isolation and helplessness, and he had no way to go, which was the same as the Han Chinese. At this time, the turbaned Temir called himself a division commander and concurrently the commander-in-chief of border defense. First, he solved a group of Han Chinese in Shache (it is said that of the thousand or so Han Chinese, only a hundred or so remained, excluding the women who were looted), and then solved the two counties of Yingjisha and Puliy (three or four Han Chinese were left in Yingjisha, and only one was left in Puliy), and sealed off the exit route (foreigners could leave freely) and strictly prohibited Han Chinese from entering or leaving. We Han Chinese had long anticipated today's disaster and were willing to leave Kashgar as soon as possible. Before the rebel party reached Aksu, we repeatedly asked the Kashgar authorities to issue passports, but they were not approved (foreigners were an exception). It is not known what their intentions were. Now that the power of the turbaned bandits has grown, we only earnestly beg the central government to quickly send a large force of Han Chinese troops to Xinjiang to quell the rebellion. According to the investigation, the actual number of troops of the Buyi and turbaned parties in Kashgar is no more than 5,000 in total, and there is a severe shortage of guns and bullets (there are not enough 3,000 guns, and most of them are old-fashioned rifles). Recently, they have been in contact with the British Consulate in Kashgar, intending to purchase from Britain. The British Consulate refused because it did not have government permission. Moreover, their troops are all a mob, with no training. This time, taking advantage of the chaos, they have already plundered the wealth and women of the Han Chinese, and many do not want to be soldiers.

Page 12

The military strength is decreasing rather than increasing, and the internal organization is also disorganized. If 100,000 regular troops are used (50,000 or 60,000 is also possible, but less is not enough for control), the rebellion in the entire Xinjiang province can be put down immediately. However, we must take decisive measures to cut the mess quickly. The sooner the better. If we continue to hesitate, the snipe and clam will fight, and the fisherman will benefit. I fear that Xinjiang will not be ours for long. (July 20th)

Jiangsu Province Canal Dredging Project Officially Begins Today 84

Chairman Chen and Others Travel by Special Boat to Huai'an to Preside Over the Opening Ceremony

Zhenjiang News: The Jiangsu Province canal dredging project into the sea, originally scheduled to officially commence on October 10th, was repeatedly postponed due to lack of funding. It was not until the end of September that funding was secured. The project office actively prepared on October 1st. The original construction plan stipulated that workers from all counties should be recruited by October 15th, and construction sections should also be established by October 15th. Subsequently, due to the provincial government convening a meeting of county heads in the canal dredging area, the deadline was extended to the 20th. Further delays arose due to various difficulties, with the final decision to officially begin work today (the 1st). Provincial Government Chairman Chen Guofu, accompanied by Civil Affairs Director Yu Jingtang, Construction Director Shen Baixian, and others, crossed the Yangtze River on the afternoon of the day before yesterday (the 30th), traveling by special boat to Huai'an to preside over the opening ceremony and inspect the engineering design. A summary of Chief Engineer Ge's first-phase plan for dredging the canal into the sea and the implementation steps are as follows:

(A) Regarding Calculation Aspects: The Yellow River's old course to be dredged this time connects the Zhangfu Diversion River from Hongze Lake in the north to the Taizikou outlet to the sea in the south, totaling more than 160 kilometers in length. From Yangzhuang to Qitao, the old embankments are mostly utilized, while below Qitao, an entirely new river channel is to be constructed. The original planned riverbed width was 120 meters, but the initial phase of construction has been revised to 35 meters, with side slopes of 1:2.5 and a top width of 230 meters (originally planned at 350 meters). The riverbed height is stipulated to be 7.5 meters below the flood level, while Taizikou is 6 meters below sea level. The gradient decreases by 7.05 centimeters per thousand meters. Using the Francis formula to calculate the flow rate, at a Hongze Lake water level of 13.5 meters, the discharge rate is 319 cubic meters per second; at 15 meters, it is 485 cubic meters per second; and at 15.5 meters, it is 550 cubic meters per second. According to current measurements, the abandoned Yellow River has no discharge when the water level is at 13 meters. Now that the Three Rivers active dam will be built, the normal water level of Hongze Lake will consistently be at 13.5 meters. Before major floods occur, the waterway to the sea can first be used for drainage, emptying Hongze Lake's water storage, thus reducing the impact of autumn floods. The excavation depth for the entire project ranges from a minimum of 6 meters to a maximum of 12 meters, with an average depth of over 8 meters. The earthwork is estimated at over 60 million cubic meters, with an average subsidy of eight cents of silver per cubic meter. Including the cost of materials, water removal equipment, and management, the total cost is estimated at seven million silver dollars, to be implemented over two years. In the first year, over 30 million cubic meters should be completed, requiring approximately half of the total budget.

(B) Regarding Implementation Aspects: Surveying work, from mid-July to October 7th, was completed with the full support of the canal dredging committee's surveying team. Over 3,000 cross-sectional diagrams were drawn, and the new river channel was plotted on topographical maps. The area of the new cross-sections for river slopes was calculated separately, and finally, the amount of earthwork was tabulated and distributed to each section. The sections were then divided into two categories: Huaiyin with 20,000 workers over 22.762 kilometers; Siyang with 10,000 workers over 11.22 kilometers; Jiangdu with 5,000 workers over 4.192 kilometers; Taixian with 5,000 workers over 4.597 kilometers; Gaoyou with 10,000 workers over 10.234 kilometers; Baoying with 10,000 workers over 11.36 kilometers; Huaian with 20,000 workers over 22.42 kilometers; Lianshui with 25,000 workers over 22.625 kilometers; Xinghua with 10,000 workers over 10.287 kilometers; Dongtai with 5,000 workers over 3.289 kilometers; and Yancheng with 15,000 workers over 22.843 kilometers, totaling 160,000 workers over 162 kilometers. The bottom five kilometers of sea entrance beach cutting will be considered separately. In the third step of organizing the workers, each county will organize a general team, managed by the county government, with construction personnel as the general team leader. Districts will be divided into several brigades, each brigade with 1,000 people, led by a brigade commander, with platoon leaders below, each platoon with 100 people. Brigade commanders and platoon leaders will be appointed by the county magistrate from local self-governance personnel, under the command of the general team leader. Each platoon is divided into four squads, each squad with 25 people, with one foreman, who will use each squad or platoon to excavate an earth pond, measuring the work completed. As for maintaining order, in addition to the worker regulations, the county will dispatch a security team to protect everything at the construction site. Other matters concerning the workers' clothing, food, housing, and transportation are fully prepared. In the fourth step, regarding the water pumping project, on average, a small section of the new river channel will be excavated every eight kilometers, or a suitable location will be selected for dredging and installing pumping stations, requiring approximately twenty 12-horsepower water pumps. In addition, excavation methods will be used to allow the water to naturally drain away, with each worker equipped with water buckets to supplement the machine power. (31st)

Organizational Outline of the War Zone Consolidation Committee 85

Presiding Over the Settlement of Post-War Matters in the War Zone

The Twelve-Article Outline Has Been Announced

Beiping Correspondence: Post-war matters, both domestic and foreign, in the war zone have been handled through repeated consultations between the Political Reorganization Committee, the Military Subcommittee, and the Hebei Provincial Government, without a unified organization. After Huang Fu's return north recently, to unify authority and facilitate the settlement of the war zone, a War Zone Settlement Committee was established to specialize in this matter. The Political Reorganization Committee drafted the measures and submitted them to the Executive Yuan for approval, with the official establishment set for November 1st. It is projected that the settlement of post-war matters in the counties of the war zone will be completed within six months. The seven committee members have been reported previously. The committee's headquarters are temporarily located within the Political Reorganization Committee. The organizational outline has been announced, with the original text as follows:

Organizational Outline of the War Zone Settlement Committee 86

Article 1: The Executive Yuan's Beiping Political Affairs Reorganization Committee, to settle post-war matters in the counties of the war zone, has temporarily established the War Zone Settlement Committee to handle the following matters: 1. Receiving matters in the war zone; 2. Local diplomatic negotiations in the war zone; 3. Reorganizing security forces and local police in the war zone; 4. Improving administration in the counties of the war zone; 5. Rectifying local security in the war zone; 6. Coordinating local transportation in the war zone; 7. Investigating and handling various special rights matters. Article 2: This committee, based on the needs of the situation, may draft various settlement and improvement measures for implementation. Article 3: This committee shall have seven members, appointed by the Executive Yuan's Beiping Political Affairs Reorganization Committee, with three designated as standing committee members. Article 4: This committee shall have one chief secretary, and several secretaries and clerks, all of whom will be transferred from the Executive Yuan's Beiping Political Affairs Reorganization Committee. The detailed rules for the operation of this committee will be determined separately. Article 5: This committee may appoint consultants as needed. Article 6: This committee shall hold at least two meetings per month. The rules of procedure will be determined separately. Article 7: This committee shall submit monthly work reports to the Executive Yuan's Beiping Political Affairs Reorganization Committee for record. Article 8: The working period of this committee is set for six months. Article 9: The expenses of this committee shall be estimated and submitted to the Executive Yuan's Beiping Political Affairs Reorganization Committee for approval. Article 10: This committee is located in Beiping. Article 11: If there are any matters not covered in this organizational outline, they may be submitted for revision. Article 12: This organizational outline shall take effect from the date of its promulgation. (October 30th)

Wang Chonghui Meets Chiang Twice in Beiping 87

Speaks to the Press

Beiping Correspondence: National Party Central Supervisory Committee member and Judge of the Hague International Court of Justice, Wang Chonghui, after arriving in Beiping, has met with Chairman Chiang twice. Wang also received the press at the Beijing Hotel at 5:30 PM today (30th), making the following important remarks:

Thoughts on Coming North 88

I have been away from Beiping for seven years. My impressions upon returning can be divided into two points: First, seven or eight years ago, the capital was in Beiping, so everything was more prosperous. Now that the capital has moved south, the city's condition is naturally depressed. However, there have been definite achievements in municipal construction. Second, the situation in Beiping as reported in the newspapers when I was abroad is very different from the impression I get from experiencing it firsthand. I am traveling back and forth between the north and south in a private capacity to convey messages to all parties. After arriving in Beiping, I have already met Chairman Chiang twice and plan to see him again tomorrow. After returning to Shanghai, I will pack my bags and prepare to return to The Hague at the end of the year to take up my duties.

Discusses Diplomacy 89

Someone asked me about my predictions for the future trend of diplomacy in North China. In my opinion, diplomacy is a whole, and it is difficult to give a satisfactory answer in a very short time. As for the situation between Japan and Russia, in my view, both sides may be able to get along for the time being due to the railway sales issue. Regarding the pseudo-Manchukuo oil sales issue, this matter fundamentally violates the Washington Treaty's two major principles: 1. Equal opportunity; 2. Open door. Judging by common sense, it cannot become a reality. This can be asserted.

Leaving Southward Soon 90

Wang continued, saying that he would stay in Beiping for another day or two before going south to Shanghai. Whether he would make another trip to the southwest would depend on whether it was necessary. Assuming that he did not need to go to the southwest, he would definitely return to The Hague at the end of the year because he still had two months of vacation, and so on. (30th)

Kunshan

Zhengyang Bridge Reconstruction Completed 92

Zhengyang Bridge, outside Chaoyangmen on the road, is the main road in and out of the city. Originally made of wood, it has been dilapidated for ten years. Three months ago, the road company spent 13,000 yuan to rebuild it with copper-bone cement. It was contracted by the Shanghai Qiao Yu and Construction Factory. After construction started, the bridge was built day and night and has now been completed. At 10:00 AM on the 28th, a completion ceremony was held for the bridge. The road company hosted people from all walks of life at Yushan Elementary School to visit. The guests were very enthusiastic.

Changshu

Drought Relief Association Distributes Wheat Seed Loans 93

The county's Drought Relief Committee decided to allocate 10,000 yuan to purchase wheat seeds for loans to farmers in the disaster areas. It is currently underway, and the methods are as follows: 1. The loan area is limited to the cotton fields in the disaster-stricken areas of the second, fifth, sixth, and third districts; 2. The loan farmers are limited to poor households within each district who cannot afford to buy wheat seeds; 3. The reporting method is that the township chiefs first investigate the actual number of fields, the amount of seeds, and the detailed names and addresses of the poor farmers. Report to the district office for collection and forwarding for verification and distribution; 4. The loan method is that each district prints and distributes loan certificates to be filled out and stamped by the township office and distributed; 5. The repayment period is May of the 24th year of the Republic of China, and each township is responsible for collecting the payments and returning them in full.

Wuxi

Mediation Resolves Agricultural Bank Warehouse Issue 94

Local rice, bean, and miscellaneous grain merchants, due to the Farmers Bank operating warehouses and engaging in transportation and sales, which conflicted with their business, were about to be taken over entirely. Therefore, they specifically proposed a discussion at the members' meeting of the County Chamber of Commerce, requesting a way to remedy the situation. The County Chamber of Commerce, on the previous day, invited leaders of the rice and grain industry and representatives of the Farmers Bank to discuss and mediate. As a result, the Farmers Bank agreed that agricultural warehouses would only accept and dispose of agricultural products directly entrusted by farmers themselves, or purchased by the Jiangsu Provincial Government. They would not accept products with the purpose of intermediate profit. The rice industry stated that if the Farmers Bank's involvement in transportation and sales benefited farmers and did not involve intermediate profit, they were willing to handle it on behalf of the bank within the possible range, following the pawnshop method. With this mutual agreement, the dispute was completely resolved.

Hua Juchu Re-examined and Found Not Addicted 95

Hua Juchu, Director of General Affairs of the Tobacco and Alcohol Public Monopoly Inspection Office, was previously accused by peddler Wang Jiugeng of smoking opium without a license. After the county's drug rehabilitation center conducted an initial examination, based on the report of Director Gu, he was found to have no drug addiction. Wang Zuogeng was dissatisfied and requested the County Anti-Opium Association to allow a joint re-examination. On the 22nd of last month, the association sent both parties to the county's drug rehabilitation center for a re-examination. As of the morning of the 30th, the period had expired. The results of the re-examination still showed no drug addiction. The Chief of General Affairs, Hua Hongshou, held a hearing and ordered Hua Juchu to submit the original guarantee, and Wang Zuogeng was detained. Wang again declared his dissatisfaction, saying that during the re-examination period, Hua Juchu was still eating supplements. One day, Hua was hungry and asked for something to eat at the center, without specifying what. Unexpectedly, the center gave him a bowl of candied lotus seeds to satisfy his hunger. This was very suspicious and requested that he be transferred to the provincial level for re-examination, or sent to the Zhenru Forensic Institute for re-examination, so that the truth could come out. Now, Wang Zuogeng has applied to be escorted to the provincial level for re-examination, and has also accused Gu Zengliang, the director of the County Drug Rehabilitation Center, of malpractice in the examination, requesting his dismissal and investigation.

Large-Scale Opium Den Broken Up 96

The Public Security Bureau's Inspection Office received a secret report the night before yesterday that a large-scale opium dealer, Yang Chunxiang, was selling private opium at No. 13 Fenghuang Bridge Street, No. 24 Zhuyuan Lane, Zhou Shanbang, and No. 79 Baiyi Port outside the South Gate, managed by his mistresses Zhu Miao and Deng Miao, and his father Yang Qing, respectively. They requested their arrest. Chief Inspector Wang dispatched personnel to investigate in disguise and confirmed the report. At dawn yesterday, he personally led the police to search and arrest them. In No. 13 Fenghuang Bridge Street, they seized 107 taels of high-quality Yunnan opium, as well as wire baskets, chops, receipts for extortion, silver dollars, and other items, and arrested Zhu Miao. However, the main suspect, Yang Chunxiang, managed to escape. The police searched the 21 neighboring houses completely, but could not find him. They then went to No. 79 Baiyi Port and seized one catty of old Lantian opium, 44 taels of high-quality Yunnan opium, 3 catties and 10 taels of cake opium, as well as chops, scissors, silver dollars, and other items, and arrested Deng Miao. They then went to No. 24 Zhuyuan Lane, Zhou Shanbang, and seized opium scales, opium wrapping paper, silver dollars, and other items, and arrested Yang Qing. Later, they found that No. 23 next door was also Yang's opium trafficking contact point. They immediately entered and arrested Zhao Shilong, as well as banknotes, silver dollars, and other items, and took them all to the bureau to be handed over to the County Anti-Opium Association for legal action.

Changzhou

Chamber of Commerce Discusses New Stamp Tax Issue 97

The Wuyi County Chamber of Commerce convened leaders from various industries on the afternoon of the 30th to discuss the issue of affixing the new stamp tax. Acting Chairman Xu Juxi presided over the discussion. The matters discussed included: 1. The new stamp tax is scheduled to be implemented on November 1st. The registration and exchange methods for the old stamp tax have not yet been announced. How should we express our opinion on this? It was resolved that stamp tax is a valuable security of the government. The chamber of commerce and merchants in this county affix stamp tax, which is related to actual affixing, and is different from those who recognize and sell them. The chamber of commerce and merchants should not suffer losses. Before the registration and exchange methods for the old stamp tax are announced, the implementation of the new stamp tax will be temporarily suspended. The chamber of commerce will telegraph the Ministry of Finance to inquire and announce the registration and exchange methods, and request the county government to temporarily suspend inspection to maintain public trust and alleviate merchants' difficulties. 2. The newly established stamp tax law adopts a progressive system, which merchants cannot afford. How should we express our opinion on this? It was resolved to telegraph the Legislative Yuan, the Executive Yuan, and the Ministry of Finance to maintain the original plan.

Yangzhou

At the county's third county-wide administrative meeting, Yan Zhiqin and others proposed the proposal that the disaster victims in the eighth and ninth districts are crying out for food, how should we find ways to provide relief, and Xu Hongliang and others proposed the proposal to investigate the accumulated grain to prepare for disaster relief.
