Dai Chunfeng's International Honor in Calligraphy 190

Mr. Dai Chunfeng, a member of the Shanghai French Municipal Council, was formerly a senior employee of the Sino-French National Institute of Technology. He was relied upon by the authorities for more than ten years. He retired due to illness. Mr. Dai, in the midst of his busy official duties, never abandoned his ambition to practice calligraphy. For nearly twenty years, people knew that he was meticulous in his work and enthusiastic about public welfare, but they did not know that he was an expert in epigraphy. He did not easily show his work to others, so only his closest friends could see it. In 1930, his calligraphy was sent to Belgium and won a gold medal after international judging. This year, at the American Exposition, he sent nearly 40 styles of Jinshi calligraphy from the Qin and Han dynasties, which were displayed by the association to promote culture and show the evolution of Chinese characters throughout the ages, and to attract the attention of expatriates. It is said that the works in the United States have already been snapped up by the audience. Mr. Dai can be said to be highly valued and has opened a new record in the contemporary art world.

To the Editor: Regarding today's (31st) issue of your esteemed newspaper, in the "Local News" section, the article "The Rising Trend of Water Diversion Expands, Shipping Companies Decide to Suspend Navigation," the last paragraph of the National News Agency's draft mentions a "Navigation Bureau meeting," which is not in accordance with the facts. Page 18

Commemorative Publication for the Commencement of Work on Dredging and Diverting the Huai River into the Sea

— Inscribed by Chen Guofu

Essays

The Motivation Behind Jiangsu Province's Conscription of Labor for the Preliminary Project of Dredging and Diverting the Huai River into the Sea 200

— Chen Guofu

For nearly a century, the counties in the Huai River basin of this province have suffered immense losses in lives and property due to repeated floods. Although there are no precise statistics for verification, the severity of the harm is well-known to those who have grown up in this land and are familiar with the history of the Huai River basin. Official and private records also detail it extensively. Without discussing the distant past, recently, in 1931, the Huai River swelled violently, causing more than forty breaches in the eastern and western embankments of the Grand Canal. Over ten counties in the Lixiahe region were completely submerged in floodwaters. Considering only the losses in crop yields and property, it already amounted to tens of millions of yuan, not to mention the sacrifices of human and animal lives, and homes. Because of the inadequacy of human efforts, the people of several dozen counties north of the Yangtze River tremble in fear at the slightest sign of a Huai River surge, running around in panicked sweat, yet remain helpless. They can only hope to escape with their lives by some stroke of luck. Is this not an utterly lamentable situation?

During the late Qing dynasty, Ding Xian of Huai'an first proposed the idea of dredging the Huai River. Later, Zhang Jian of Nantong further elaborated on this idea, attracting the keen attention of concerned individuals. Unfortunately, disputes over the route to the sea or the Yangtze River remained unresolved. Coupled with frequent political instability and significant financial challenges, various factors created obstacles, and it could not be implemented. However, the importance of the Huai River dredging project and the urgency of public demand became increasingly evident. Since 1929, the central government has established the Huai River Dredging Commission specifically for this purpose, with leaders of the party and the nation serving as its heads. The importance attached to the Huai River dredging project is evident. After several years of research and investigation, taking into account the proposals of predecessors, widely soliciting public opinion, and further verifying with on-site surveys, the grand plan of diverting water separately into the Yangtze and the sea was finalized. In terms of engineering plans, it can be said that a stage has been reached. As long as the funding is secured, large-scale construction will not be difficult.

Although the Huai River dredging project concerns the four provinces of Shandong, Henan, Anhui, and Jiangsu, the three provinces of Shandong, Henan, and Anhui are located upstream. Without the dredging of the Huai River, the discharge of water will only be slightly less smooth. This province, however, is situated at the tail end of the Huai River, receiving water from all three provinces. With no outlet for the water, the fertile land of several dozen counties in the Huai River basin is forced to serve as a collection point for the floodwaters of the upstream three provinces. The extent of the harm is beyond description. The Huai River Dredging Commission is planning for the long term, and its overall planning must be far-reaching. Before the entire budget is secured, starting large-scale construction will inevitably take time. However, the livelihood issues of the counties north of the Yangtze River in this province are of utmost importance and cannot be delayed any longer. This is the first reason why we must first undertake the preliminary project of diverting the river into the sea to eliminate the scourge as soon as possible.

This province has long been known as a region of abundant wealth in the southeast, rich in products and flourishing in commerce. However, in recent years, repeated droughts and floods have plagued the area, leading to economic hardship for industry and commerce, and the rural economy is increasingly heading towards bankruptcy. Bandits are lurking, and refugees are everywhere. The main reason for this is the neglect of water conservancy, and the failure to dredge the Huai River north of the Yangtze River is the crux of the problem. If we do not plan for this now, what endless troubles will there be in the future? When I first arrived in Jiangsu last year, I was deeply concerned and believed that completing the dredging of the Huai River was a crucial task for rescuing the people's livelihood north of the Yangtze River. At the same time, because the Huai River dredging project requires tens of millions of yuan, which the current financial resources of this province cannot afford, I proposed the idea of conscripting labor to carry out the preliminary project of diverting the river into the sea. Although there is an ancient saying about using the strength of the people, there was still some doubt whether the project was too large to be carried out smoothly. This spring, we slightly repaired and dredged the Liutang River, relying on the labor of the people in the counties along the river, and the gentry worked together to assist, and it was completed as scheduled. It was then that I realized that the people in the Huai River basin are indeed capable of great things. This is the second reason why we resolutely adopted the method of conscripting labor to carry out the preliminary project of dredging and diverting the Huai River into the sea.

Some may argue that the Huai River dredging project is a matter of national importance, and the central government must bear this heavy responsibility. The project is difficult and expensive, and only the central government has the resources to complete it. In a time when the finances of this province are already stretched, we should not force the people to exert their strength and do it piecemeal. I disagree. The Huai River dredging project takes the relief of the people's livelihood as a prerequisite. The responsibility belongs to the central government, but the benefits remain with the local area. Although the central government feels that it is not easy to raise a large sum of money due to the serious national crisis, it has also used the Boxer Indemnity funds to start preliminary projects such as the Zhangfu River. The completion of the Huaiyin Shaobo Liujian three sluices is under construction, the preparation of the Sanheba Dam project, and the repair of the west embankment of the Grand Canal, etc. The cost of these projects is thousands and millions of yuan. If we further supplement what the central government cannot reach with the local people's strength and financial resources of this province and proceed jointly, it will be of a cooperative nature with the central government, and it will still be a self-rescue plan for this province. With internal and external support, and joint efforts, the results will be easily seen, and success can be expected.

Moreover, I have even greater hopes. The Huai River dredging project concerns four provinces. This province is located downstream. Although the three upstream provinces do not have the intention of using their neighbors as a drain, this province has suffered repeated disasters and suffered greater pain because it receives water from the three provinces. Now, this province, after repeated disasters and financial difficulties, has already borne the burden of pain and taken the initiative to carry out the preliminary project of dredging and diverting the Huai River into the sea. I especially hope that the three upstream provinces will do their best to assist, and the central government will lead the organization to lead, so that the great project can be completed as soon as possible. I cannot help but wait and see!

The Process of Preparing for the Preliminary Project of Dredging and Diverting the Huai River into the Sea 201

— Shen Baixian

The Huai River originally flowed into the sea independently, and was listed as one of the "Four Rivers." Since the time of Yu the Great's flood control, it has remained unchanged for more than three thousand years. From the Five Dynasties and Northern Song onwards, the Yellow River broke its banks and caused problems for the Huai River. During the Yuan and Ming dynasties, Jia Lu blocked the breaches, and Liu Daxia built the Taihang Dike. The Huai River was thus taken over by the Yellow River, stopping at every gate, taking Hongze and Gaobao Lakes as temporary lodgings, and the Eastern Sluice Dams for self-transportation into the Yangtze River and the sea as its final resting place. Thus, between Huai'an and Yangzhou, the disasters of the Huai River have occurred repeatedly, and have not ended to this day. In the fifth year of Xianfeng (1855), the Yellow River broke at Tongwaxiang and moved north, returning to the old course of Qiancheng. The proposal to dredge the Huai River arose accordingly. Mr. Ding Xipu of Shanyang was the first to advocate for it, and knowledgeable individuals responded in unison. During the reigns of Guangxu and Xuantong, Mr. Zhang Jian of Nantong advocated even more vigorously. By the time of the Republic of China, the Jianghuai Water Conservancy Survey Bureau was established, later renamed the Huai River Dredging Survey Office. The achievements from the survey from the first year of the Republic of China (1912) to the fifteenth year (1926) were most notable. The late Premier's "National Construction Plan" further recognized the dredging of the Huai River as an urgent matter. The Second Plenary Session of the Kuomintang, adhering to the legacy, resolved to implement dredging based on the survey results of the past eighteen years. The Central Government immediately established the Huai River Dredging Commission, aiming to complete the project within a specified period to eliminate the disaster of the Huai River and secure the people's livelihood. Looking back over the past seventy or eighty years, the Chinese people have exhausted their efforts to realize the dredging of the Huai River, and their diligence can be said to be thorough. However, they have long been troubled by the cost of labor, resulting in empty words without any benefit. Now, I, Baixian, following Chairman Chen, have been appointed to manage the construction of Jiangsu Province, and after taking office, I was ordered to prepare for the conscription of labor to carry out the preliminary project of diverting the Huai River into the sea. I am secretly pleased that the most desired thing of the Chinese people can be realized. Now that the preparations have been completed and the great project will begin immediately, I will describe the preparation process as a memorial to the beginning of the project.

The Huai River dredging work has been painstakingly carried out by the Huai River Dredging Commission for several years, considering the opinions of all parties, surveying, researching, and finally determining the principle of separating the Yangtze River and the sea. The waterway into the sea runs from the Zhangfu River through the abandoned Yellow River to the Taozikou to enter the sea. The original plan was for a bottom width of 120 meters and a dike distance of 350 meters, requiring a cost of more than 34 million yuan. The work is large and expensive, and it is definitely not something that the provincial government's finances can afford. Therefore, last year, we first conscripted labor to dredge the Liutang River as a preparation and experiment for the Huai River dredging project. We relied on the enthusiastic conscription of the people and the enthusiastic assistance of the gentry, and the result was exceptionally satisfactory. It was then that we became certain that the elders and brothers of the Huai River basin understood the principles and were able to bravely do what was just and not complain when it came to matters of vital interest; this is why the decision was made to conscript labor to carry out the Huai River into the sea project.

In May of this year, the General Office had a two-year plan for the first phase of the Huai River into the sea project. The river line runs from the Zhangfu River along the abandoned Yellow River channel to the Qitao, leaving the abandoned Yellow River and entering the sea from the Taozikou. The total length is about 172 kilometers, and the distance between the two dikes is 350 meters. Except for the bottom width of the river, which is reduced from 120 meters to 35 meters, everything else is handled in accordance with the original plan of the Huai River Commission. It is estimated that more than 66.6 million cubic meters of earth need to be excavated and more than 5 million cubic meters of earth need to be used for building dikes, all of which will be done by conscripting labor. In order to consider the work, food expenses will still be given appropriately according to the square, which is estimated to cost more than 6.8 million yuan. As for the two movable dams at Yangzhuang and Zhoumen, which require a cost of 1.06 million yuan, they will still be undertaken by the Huai River Commission in order to achieve division of labor and cooperation, and to have both storage and discharge.

In June of this year, after the Liutang River project was completed, the Huai River Dredging Commission was immediately consulted to order the relevant counties to continue to open up the Huai River into the sea waterway by conscripting labor. The original consultation stated briefly:

The route for opening up the waterway into the sea has recently been agreed upon by the Chief Engineer of the Association and Director Shen of the Construction Department of your province, and the method of conscripting labor to dredge the Liutang River will be adopted. The relevant counties will be ordered to continue to open up the waterway from Yangzhuang, Huaiyin, through the abandoned Yellow River Qitao to the Taozikou by conscripting labor. Before the start of construction, a construction survey team should be organized to nail down the river line and survey the earthworks in detail as a standard for allocating labor to each county. The operating expenses of this survey team and all the necessary equipment for the staff will be prepared by this Association. The dredging project, the dike construction project, and other necessary equipment related to the project should be handled by your province by conscripting labor to comply with cooperation and reduce Shen disaster. The case was then submitted to the 669th meeting of the Provincial Government Committee, and the resolution in principle was passed. After consulting the Huai River Commission, the conscription matters will be prepared by this province, and the survey matters will be implemented quickly to facilitate progress.

In early July of this year, the Huai River Commission was approved to consult that the sea waterway survey team would depart immediately, and it was requested to order the protection of the counties under its jurisdiction. The counties along the river were ordered to comply properly, and the public security department was jointly ordered to order the military police in the counties along the river to listen to the survey team's consultation in order to be thorough.

In August of this year, this province presented to the central government for approval the issuance of 20 million yuan of water conservancy construction bonds for the purpose of preparing for the Huai River into the sea, opening up new canals, and handling drought relief and other projects. 6 million yuan was allocated to the Huai River into the sea project by conscripting labor. The most difficult problem to solve in the Huai River dredging project, the funding problem, was also solved satisfactorily at this point.

In September of this year, the survey was about to be completed, and the dredging project urgently needed to be implemented. Therefore, the draft organizational regulations for the Jiangsu Province Huai River into the Sea Engineering Office and the section engineering offices were prepared. In order to be extra cautious, the provincial government was asked to appoint the chief engineer of the Huai River Commission as a consulting engineer to guide the handling at any time. The case was submitted to the 691st meeting of the Provincial Government Committee. The resolution was to handle the appointment letter and to amend and approve the regulations. It was also resolved to appoint Xu Xinwu as the Director of the Jiangsu Province Huai River into the Sea Engineering Office, Chen Hefu as the Deputy Director, and Ge Hanlou as the Chief Engineer. The letters of appointment were issued separately by the Provincial Government. The Engineering Office was established in Huaiyin on October 1, and the construction was scheduled to begin on time. On one side, a telegram was sent to the four counties of Huaiyin, Huai'an, Lianshui, and Funing to repair and level the south embankment of the abandoned Yellow River, so that cars could travel on it to facilitate the construction work. The deadline was before October 10. The counties north of the Yangtze River were ordered to investigate and report the quantity and price of reed mats produced, so that they could be purchased for building sheds to live in. At the same time, the Provincial Government ordered the administrative inspector commissioners of the Huaiyin and Yancheng districts to concurrently serve as the supervisory commissioners of the Huai River into the sea project; the county magistrates of the twelve counties of Huaiyin, Huai'an, Lianshui, Funing, Siyang, Yangyan, Yancheng, Baoying, Gaoyou, Xinghua, Dongtai, Jiangdu, and Taixian concurrently served as the conscription commissioners of the Engineering Office. The above-mentioned counties were ordered to investigate and report the number of conscripted laborers within a limited time, and to wait for allocation and distribution.

On October 2, the Huai River into the Sea Engineering Office and the 24-month regular expenses budget for the section engineering offices were jointly prepared with the Finance Department and submitted to the 693rd meeting of the Provincial Government Committee for amendment and approval. On October 8 and 16, the county magistrates of the twelve counties of Huaiyin and others were convened to the province twice, together with the Department of Civil Affairs, to discuss the progress of the conscription of laborers and to formulate the management methods for the laborers. Regulations on rewards and punishments for conscripted laborers and a proclamation to the people were issued. At that time, the Engineering Office had been established as scheduled on October 1 and started work. All the original engineering plans were re-examined by the Engineering Office, which considered that the soil removal distance was too far according to the standard cross-section, and it was impossible to do. It was proposed to reduce the original plan of 350 meters between the two dikes to 230 meters, and the average soil removal distance was 122 meters, which was 32% shorter than the original plan, so that the number of workers and the date could meet the regulations, and there would be no impact on the amount of discharge. The consultation was transferred to the Steering Committee for approval. Thus, the Huai River into the sea project, which was initiated 70 or 80 years ago, was decided to be implemented on November 1, 1934, after half a year of preparation.

Moreover, there is something that Baixian cannot help but say: the Huai River into the sea project requires a total cost of 34 million yuan according to the original plan of the Huai River Commission, that is, the preliminary project plan this time, if it is not done by conscripting labor, it will also require 16 million yuan. Now, we resolutely use 6 million yuan to carry out a 16 million yuan project. This is because the disasters of the Huai River are urgent and cannot be delayed or hesitated; and the satisfactory results of the Liutang River project have also encouraged and promoted it. The value of the work done on the Liutang River is estimated at 1 million yuan. The provincial government raised 360,000 yuan, which only accounts for 13% of the total cost; the remaining 50% is the labor of the laborers; and 20% is the merit of the gentry's assistance. Now, the 60,000 yuan raised by the provincial government for the Huai River project is approaching 30% of the originally planned 16 million yuan; the remaining 60-70% is expected to be borne by the local elders and brothers in order to eradicate the old and hidden troubles of many years and seek a permanent and lasting peace, and they will be able to bear the pain, struggle, and work together with the government in unity; then, the completion of the project in two years as scheduled can be guaranteed. In the future, when the project is completed, the Huai and Hai Rivers will be connected, with high banks and deep channels, dispersing the turbidity and raising the clarity, and after ten or dozens of years, they will gradually return to their original state. The effect should surpass what was expected in the preliminary project: and the commencement of this preliminary project is enough to move people to remember and increase the value of commemoration!

Plans

Original Plan for the Two-Year Project of Jiangsu Province's Labor Conscription for Opening and Dredging the Huai River into the Sea 202

(I) Introduction

Since its establishment in the 18th year of the Republic of China, the Huai River Conservancy Commission has, after several surveys and designs, and discussions of gains and losses, finally decided to adopt the principle of diverting the Huai River into both the Yangtze River and the sea. The outline of the entire Huai River management plan and the plan for the waterway into the sea have been successively announced. The final decision for the waterway into the sea was to pass through the Zhangfu River, through the abandoned Yellow River, to the Taizikou to enter the sea, with a total length of approximately 172 kilometers. The river bottom width is 120 meters. The distance between the two embankments is 350 meters. The total cost required is 34,426,900 yuan. Subsequently, due to the large cost and difficulty in raising funds, a phased implementation plan was developed. The first phase of the project, except that the river bottom width was reduced from 120 meters to 35 meters, everything else remained unchanged from the original plan. However, it still required 16 million yuan in construction funds. Ultimately, due to the large scale of the project and the large amount of funds required, it was never realized.

Tracing back to the Yellow River's northward diversion, the Huai River has never returned to its original course. Our Jiangsu Province is located at the tail end of the Huai River, suffering from disasters in almost nine out of ten years. The people are struggling to survive. Therefore, local people in Jiangsu Province deeply hope that this waterway into the sea will be completed as soon as possible to alleviate the pain of the sinking of Jiangbei. The Huai River Conservancy Commission is currently actively carrying out the initial management of the Central Canal and the Li Canal project, and the funds required for the sea entry project are very large. It is deeply felt that raising funds is difficult. In order to promote the early realization of the Huai River into the sea project, the provincial government of this province intends to cooperate with the Huai River Conservancy Commission and, with reference to the method of labor conscription for repairing and dredging the Liutang River, to achieve rapid completion. At the same time, considering the difficulty of the life of the laborers, it is still planned to raise a large amount of money from the province to provide food according to the location, so as to maintain the livelihood of the laborers and enable them to work with peace of mind and jointly accomplish this great undertaking.

(II) Project Overview

The original route planned by the Huai River Conservancy Commission is extremely perfect. Taking the straightening of the bend between Yinjia Ferry and Jiaolingji as an example, not only is the amount of earthwork reduced, but the drainage is also increased due to the steeper slope. The effect is very obvious, but near the straightened bend, the terrain is low-lying and the embankment is too high. Ramming work cannot be handled by labor conscription. If a slight carelessness, the disaster of embankment collapse will be repeated. Therefore, it is necessary to make appropriate changes, still following the old channel of the abandoned Yellow River. Below Qitao, the original plan of the Huai River Conservancy Commission is still followed, and the river directly enters the sea from Taizikou to save labor costs.

The cross-section of this plan still follows the Huai River Conservancy Commission's plan. A waterway with a bottom width of 35 meters is built in the abandoned Yellow River channel according to the preliminary project of dredging the Zhangfu River to discharge floodwaters. When the water level of Hongze Lake is 15 meters, the river water depth is 7.5 meters. The top of the two embankments is 1.5 meters above the flood level, and the embankment distance is 350 meters. One movable dam each is built at Yangzhuang and Zhoumen. The water level difference between Hongze Lake and Yangzhuang is 1.4 meters. The head loss of Yangzhuang movable dam is 0.25 meters. The water level below Yangzhuang Dam is 13.35 meters, and the sea level is 1.5 meters. The head loss of the Zhoumen movable dam is 0.25 meters. Therefore, the total drop of the water surface from the downstream of Yangzhuang Dam to the sea is 11.6 meters. This plan follows the old channel of the abandoned Yellow River. The route is slightly more circuitous, with a total length of 168.59 kilometers. Therefore, the water surface gradient is 0.0000688.

The flow rate is calculated using Forchheimer's formula.

In the formula, the riverbed roughness coefficient (n) is 0.0225. The relationship between the flow rate and the water level of Hongze Lake is as follows:

Hongze Lake Water Level Riverbed Width Gradient Flow Velocity Flow Rate

From the above table, it can be seen that when the water level of Hongze Lake is 15 meters, the flow rate is 455 cubic meters per second. It is found that the maximum flow rate of the abandoned Yellow River in the 10th year of the Republic of China was 183 cubic meters per second. At that time, the water level of Yangzhuang was 15.19 meters. The maximum flow rate of the abandoned Yellow River in the 20th year of the Republic of China was 339 cubic meters per second. At that time, the water level of Yangzhuang was 15.82 meters. It is also found that when the water level of Yangzhuang is below 13.0 meters, the abandoned Yellow River has no outflow. Comparing this with the above table, the effect of excavation can be seen. If the Three Rivers movable dam at the mouth of Hongze Lake is completed, the normal water level of Hongze Lake will be 13.5 meters. Before a major flood occurs, the sea entry waterway can first be lowered as much as possible to partially empty the lake water in advance. Since Hongze Lake has this diversion waterway, its rise will be slowed down, and the chance of reaching the highest peak will also be reduced. Indirectly reducing the burden of Hongze Lake is also indirectly shortening the time of the flood peak. Therefore, after the completion of the Three Rivers movable dam, the effect of the sea entry waterway will be more significant. (See the plan view for the route)

The riverbed of the abandoned Yellow River is mostly sandy soil. After deepening, the water is sufficient, and it may be gradually expanded by hydraulic erosion, which will be more economical and efficient.

(III) Earthwork Estimate

The calculation of the earthwork in this plan is based on the actual topographic map measured by the Huaiyang Xuhai Cross-Section Survey Bureau in the 10th year of the Republic of China and the longitudinal section map of the abandoned Yellow River bed. A total of 69 cross-sections were taken. For the sake of simplicity, three points were taken from the riverbed and both banks of each cross-section, and the average excavation depth was calculated. The embankment height was also calculated by referring to the average terrain on both banks. This calculation may be slightly different from the actual situation, but the overall difference should not be too far. It can be used as a basis for estimating construction costs and allocating work sections. Once construction starts, detailed measurement and re-estimation will be carried out.

The total excavation earthwork for the entire river is 66,606,311 cubic meters, and the embankment earthwork is 5,036,090 cubic meters. All embankment work is built using excavated soil, and no foundation is added for the time being. (The earthwork calculation table is omitted)

(IV) Construction Method

The original plan of the Huai River Conservancy Commission was to build one movable dam each at Yangzhuang and Zhoumen. It is proposed that the Huai River Conservancy Commission will still be responsible for the construction. All excavation and embankment earthwork will be handled by the labor conscription of this province. The entire project is scheduled to be completed in two years so that it can be completed at the same time as the two-year construction plan of the Huai River Conservancy Commission.

The construction of the Zhoumen movable dam is entirely for controlling the water volume and raising the water level to supply irrigation water to the Funing area. Currently, the Huai River Conservancy Commission has not been able to handle shipping and irrigation east of Lixiahe for the time being. If funds are tight, the construction of the Zhoumen movable dam can be postponed. However, the Yangzhuang movable dam must be built in advance in order to control the water level of Hongze Lake and maintain the water source of the Grand Canal. Therefore, in the construction, it is planned to leave 250 meters of Yangzhuang unexcavated as the dam foundation for the construction of the movable dam and to prevent canal water from flowing in. As for the Haikou cutting beach project, it is planned to be carried out in the second year.

All laborers will be conscripted from the relevant counties along the Huai River. For the convenience of management, each county will form a section, and all will be accommodated in labor camps and work nearby. Before implementation, the amount of earthwork to be done should be calculated according to the number of laborers to be conscripted in each county. Then, the amount of earthwork shared over two years should be divided into work sections. The boundaries are designated, and the designated work sections are ordered to be completed by the county within two years. In this way, the laborers from each county will not be mixed up, and the responsibilities will be specific. The work location does not need to be moved, and the efficiency is also high.

In order to ensure that the entire project is uniform and to facilitate the guidance of technical personnel, the following 13 construction methods are specified for compliance.

Article 1: The river line should be as straight as possible and should not be curved into sharp angles. If it is unavoidable due to the terrain, there must be a curve with a radius of at least one kilometer.

Article 2: The embankment line should run parallel to the river and should be oriented in a direction that is not directly exposed to local prevailing storms.

Article 3: The river bottom width is temporarily set at 35 meters, and the river slope is uniformly 1:2.5.

Article 4: The distance between the embankments on both sides is specified as 350 meters, the embankment top width is 4 meters, and the embankment slope is uniformly 1:3.

Article 5: All excavated river soil should be used to build the embankment body.

Article 6: If there is an old embankment that does not need to be repaired or there is excess excavated soil, the remaining excavated soil should be piled outside the embankment to widen the embankment foot.

Article 7: When repairing old embankments, in addition to removing all tree bark, grass roots, and stones from the slope, it should be cut into a stepped shape, with each step being 30 centimeters high, and interlocked with the new soil layer by layer to gradually increase the height.

Article 8: When building new embankments, all tree roots, grass skin, stones, and branches and leaves of all plants in the embankment foundation must be completely removed without any residue. The old soil on the surface layer must also be loosened before adding new soil.

Article 9: All branches and grass roots in the excavated river soil must be removed.

Article 10: If the excavated river soil is too poor, it can only be used to fill the core of the embankment. The embankment top slope must be covered with good soil.

Article 11: If there are old streams, traces of landslides, or soil holes dug due to the removal of grass roots, etc., in the new embankment foundation, they should be filled firmly.

Article 12: All burrow holes on the old embankment must be carefully checked and filled firmly.

Article 13: At ferries or roads, a road slope of 1:15 should be built. If it is a new road, it should not be at right angles to the embankment body. On the river side, it should descend in the same direction as the water flow. On the land side, it should rise in the same direction as the water flow.

(V) Regulations During Construction

The total earthwork to be excavated for the entire river is 66,606,311 cubic meters, which is scheduled to be completed in two years. Approximately 33 million cubic meters must be done each year. The embankment body is built using excavated soil, which only requires a little tidying up and does not require much labor. There are 160,000 laborers. Divided into 15 sections, construction is carried out simultaneously. The distance between the embankments on both sides is specified as 350 meters, and the earth removal distance is approximately 175 meters. If each person removes 1.5 cubic meters of soil per day, it can be completed in 140 days. Adding 70 days for rain, snow, and special accidents, the entire project can be completed in seven months.

The annual project is planned to be held during the period when the water is low and the agricultural teams are available. It is estimated that the engineering office will be organized on September 1 each year to start preparations. A meeting of the county heads of the relevant counties will be convened on September 10. The engineering offices of each section will be established on October 1. It is stipulated that construction must start uniformly before October 15. All preparatory matters such as construction, surveying, allocation of work sections, signing of tree logs, construction of dams, water baling, formulation of various regulations, and conscription of laborers to support work sheds must be completed before October 15. October 15 to May 31 of the following year is the period for implementation of the work. The engineering offices of each section will be closed on June 10 of the following year. The engineering office will be closed at the end of June. The number of people does not need to be sufficient at the beginning and end, so the regular expense budget can be calculated for nine months.

(VI) Management of Laborers

This time, when conscripting labor to dredge the abandoned Yellow River, the method of staffing is stipulated to be uniform for all counties. The smallest unit is a sub-team. Each sub-team has 100 people, with one sub-team leader. Ten sub-teams form a team, totaling 1,000 laborers, with one team leader. Each county has one general team leader to command them. The sub-team leaders and team leaders are concurrently held by the district and township chiefs appointed by the county government. The general team leader is concurrently held by the director of the construction bureau, the chief of the construction section, or the chief staff member of the county government. The county head of each county is the labor conscription commissioner, supervising the team leaders to be responsible for all labor conscription and management of laborers. All labor conscription methods, in addition to referring to the regulations on river dredging by labor conscription in each county promulgated by the Construction Department, the scope of their work is now stipulated as follows:

1. Investigate and compile the labor conscription roster

2. Investigate and compile the rosters of householders, able-bodied men, and commutation fees

3. Summon laborers

4. Hire laborers on behalf of others

5. Assign laborer teams

6. Lead the laborers to the work section

7. Supervise the laborers' attendance and work progress

8. Investigate and report the number of attendees each day

9. Handle laborer hygiene matters

10. Handle security matters

11. Handle other matters related to laborer management

The general team leaders, team leaders, and sub-team leaders of each county must be stationed at the work site to supervise the progress.

(VII) Organization of the Engineering Office

For the convenience of implementation of the project, it is proposed to establish a Huai River into the Sea Engineering Office. The office will have one director in charge of all matters within the office, one chief engineer, and several engineers and deputy engineers. Under the order of the director, they will be responsible for all matters within the office, and several assistant engineers will be responsible for supervising and guiding the progress of the work of each section under the guidance of the director and chief engineer. Review and investigate and compare the achievements of the work of each section, report the progress of the work of each section every week, and matters such as the distribution of tools and work sections. Several staff members, accountants, and compensators will be responsible for the translation and transcription of documents, the receipt and storage of documents, the custody and bookkeeping of construction funds, the payment of salaries to each staff member, and the preparation of budget calculations. Outside the office, section engineering offices will be set up to handle the affairs of each work section. The division of work sections this time is not limited to the county boundary, but is controlled by the number of laborers conscripted in each county. Each county's allocated work section will have one office, for a total of twelve offices. However, the amount of labor in each county varies, and the length and size of the project vary. Therefore, the organization of each office is also slightly different. For the work sections with larger projects, such as those undertaken by Huaiyin, Huaian, Lianshui, Yancheng, and Funing counties, each will have one engineer serving concurrently as the section chief. The remaining work sections with smaller projects will only have one to two deputy engineers or assistant engineers. However, one person will be designated by the director to concurrently serve as the section chief, and will be responsible for all matters within the section under the order of the director. Within the section, there will be several technical personnel depending on the complexity of the work. Under the order of the chief, they will be responsible for measuring work sections, supervising and guiding the progress of the project, and studying and statistically implementing the achievements of the project. Several staff members and consultants will be responsible for accounting, documentation, and writing matters. The general team leader of the laborers in each county should work in the section office and be directed by the section chief of each section.

(VIII) Budget Estimate

The unit price of the food allowance for each cubic meter of excavated earth is temporarily calculated at 8 cents per cubic meter. The total earthwork for two years is 66,606,311 cubic meters, requiring labor costs of 5,328,505 yuan. In addition, the Haikou cutting beach project costs 100,000 yuan. The total earthwork cost is 5,428,505 yuan.

The cost of dam construction and demolition is estimated at 35,000 yuan per year, and the cost of water baling is estimated at 30,000 yuan per year. All laborers will be accommodated in tents. Ten people per tent. The cost of materials for each tent is estimated at 4.5 yuan, and the annual tent construction cost is estimated at 72,000 yuan. The length of the work site is approximately 90 kilometers per year. 40 planks are used per kilometer, and each plank costs 5 yuan, for a total of 18,000 yuan. The cost of tree logs, ropes, rulers, and all other work sundries is estimated at 13,000 yuan per year. In addition, the cost of construction measurement is approximately 10,000 yuan per year. The total cost of equipment and facilities is 338,000 yuan.

There are 1,600 sub-team leaders. Each person receives a monthly allowance of 10 yuan. There are 160 team leaders. Each person receives a monthly allowance of 20 yuan. There are 15 general team leaders. Each person receives a monthly allowance of 40 yuan. Calculated for seven months per year, the total allowance is 138,600 yuan. The total cost for two years is 277,200 yuan.

The regular expenses of the engineering office and the office are budgeted for nine months per year, costing 264,855 yuan. The total cost for two years is 529,710 yuan.

The budget fee is calculated as 4% of the total budget amount. The total cost for two years is approximately 240,000 yuan. The total cost of all the above expenses is 6,813,415 yuan. In addition, two movable dams will be built at Yangzhuang and Zhoumen, costing approximately 1,060,000 yuan. It is proposed to request the Huai River Conservancy Commission to allocate funds for construction.

The annual expenses required are listed in the attached table.

It is found that the above plan is the original plan proposed by the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Construction in May of this year. As the project is currently being implemented, it has been slightly modified from time to time. This is hereby noted. Editor's Note

Special Report

Regulations for the Organization of the Huai River into the Sea Engineering Office of Jiangsu Province 203

Article 1: The Jiangsu Provincial Government, in order to jointly handle the conscription of labor for the Huai River into the Sea project with the Huai River Conservancy Commission, has established the Huai River into the Sea Engineering Office of Jiangsu Province (hereinafter referred to as the Office) directly under the Provincial Government.

Article 2: The Office shall have one Director to manage all matters of the Office, one Deputy Director and one Chief Engineer to assist the Director in handling all matters, three Engineers, four Deputy Engineers, and several Assistant Engineers and Clerks, who shall be responsible for various businesses under the order of the superior.

Article 3: The Director, Deputy Director, and Chief Engineer shall be appointed by the Provincial Government, and the Engineers shall be selected by the Director and appointed by the Provincial Government. The rest shall be selected and appointed by the Director and reported to the Provincial Government for record.

Article 4: The Office may employ employees as needed for business purposes.

Article 5: The Office may establish section engineering offices for the convenience of engineering progress, and the regulations for their organization shall be determined separately.

Article 6: The Office may establish a finance team to handle financial matters related to the project, and the detailed rules for its operation shall be determined separately.

Article 7: The labor conscription offices and the administrative supervisors of each district shall be concurrently appointed by the Provincial Government as supervision committee members to assist the Office in handling supervision matters.

Article 8: The labor conscription offices and the county heads of each county shall be concurrently appointed by the Provincial Government as labor conscription committee members of the Office, and shall handle the labor conscription matters of their respective counties under the command of the Office.

Article 9: These regulations shall be deliberated and promulgated by the Jiangsu Provincial Government Committee.

Detailed Construction Rules of the Huai River into the Sea Engineering Office 204

— (Ordered by the Engineering Office)

(A) Plan 1. This project is scheduled to be completed in two years. At the end of the first year, the excavated river shapes of each section must be connected to each other to facilitate flow.

2. Before the start of construction of each section, the section engineer shall lead the engineer, supervisor, and construction worker to actually measure the river channel map according to the prescribed standard cross-section map, nail the center tree and river bottom tree, and use lime lines to mark the excavation range, the left and right slopes, and nail the slope tree to mark the embankment and soil heap boundaries. The true height of all fixed water level posts and log posts in the section should be accurately measured initially, and should be corrected at any time thereafter.

3. The river line should be measured and taken straight, and should not be curved into sharp angles. If it is unavoidable due to the terrain, there must be a curve with a radius of at least one kilometer. The embankment line should run parallel to the river and should be oriented in a direction that is not directly exposed to local prevailing storms.

4. The river bottom width is uniformly 35 meters, and the slope of the two banks is 2.5 to 1, which means that the horizontal distance is 2.5 and the vertical distance is 1. The center distance between the two embankments is 230 meters. The planned embankment top width is 4 meters, the two slopes are 3 to 1, and the embankment is expected to be 1.5 meters higher than the flood level and 9 meters higher than the river bottom. If there is a lot of soil, the embankment body should be widened outward, and the center distance should also be lengthened. When excavating 7 meters of soil, the width of the entire river center at the embankment foot should be kept above 107 meters.

5. The engineering personnel of each section should first examine the terrain of each section, plan the drainage method, first order the laborers to draw and excavate the drainage ditch, concentrate the rainwater, select a suitable location to install a machine to pump water, or use manual water baling. If it is possible to use the order of excavation to automatically empty the stored water, efforts should be made to avoid mechanical water pumping.

6. The excavation procedure of each section is assumed as shown in the following figures (figures omitted). The engineering personnel of each section should still consider the local situation and try to select and allocate resources. The standard is that the soil removal is convenient, the rainwater has a destination, and the work is not hindered, and it is convenient to collect the earthwork.

(B) Soil Removal 7. All excavated river soil should be used to build the embankment body and should not be discarded arbitrarily. If there are old embankments and high ridges that hinder soil transportation, they should be removed first to increase the efficiency of soil removal.

8. If there is too much excavated river soil and there is a surplus in building the embankment, the soil should be piled outside the embankment as much as possible to widen the embankment foot. The soil should not be piled higher than 2 meters above the specified height.

9. If there is not enough excavated river soil to build the embankment, soil should be taken from the embankment interior, the bank beach surface, and the embankment should be built at least 30 meters from the embankment foot. The specified height should be increased by a virtual height of 20%. The earthwork for this embankment construction should be collected according to the lower side.

(C) Earthwork Calculation 10. The excavation earthwork is temporarily scheduled to be collected once a week. Before the earthwork is collected, the laborers should properly keep the remaining tree logs and marks, and repair and excavate the earth pit neatly for calculation. The supervisor should strictly check the earth pit to prevent any malpractices such as edging, capping, arching the heart, arching the waist, and steep corners.

11. The average allowance for excavating river soil is temporarily set at 8 cents per cubic meter. Because the excavation depth changes from shallow to deep and the work efficiency is very different, the unit price of the allowance is layered as shown in the table on the left.

(Note) The average beach surface should be calculated by averaging the height of the beach surface and the old river bottom in the excavated part of each small section.

12. The supervisor should pay attention to whether the laborer's soil removal complies with the regulations. If the soil removal location does not match and the soil is discarded along the way, the laborer should be ordered to carry the soil back. Otherwise, the earthwork shall not be collected.

13. When the supervisor collects the earthwork, he should fill in the team name of the sub-team, the number of laborers actually working, the number of working days, the earth pit number, and the detailed dimensions, average depth, and fill in the main collection form to calculate the earthwork. The form should be submitted to the engineer or assistant engineer for review and correction, and a wage voucher should be filled out and handed over to the team leader to be signed by the section chief at the section engineering office. The form should be stored and transferred separately, and then taken to the section accounting office to fill out a formal receipt to receive the allowance and wage.

(D) Engineering Practice 14. When excavating river soil to a considerable depth, the laborers should make slopes with more than four slopes on both slopes for easy carrying. When building embankments and heaping soil, the soil should be laid on the embankment foot first and then the embankment foot should be formed. The soil should be poured to form the embankment foot, and the height should be increased layer by layer. No planks should be used.

15. When repairing old embankments, in addition to removing all tree bark, grass roots, and stones from the slope, it should be cut into a stepped shape, with each certificate being 30 meters high, and interlocked with the new soil layer by layer to gradually increase the height.

16. When building new embankments, all tree roots, grass skin, stones, and branches and leaves of all plants in the embankment foundation must be completely removed without any residue. The old soil on the surface layer must also be loosened before adding new soil.

17. All branches, grass roots, and debris in the excavated river soil must be picked up. If the soil quality is too poor, it can only be used to fill the core of the embankment. The top surface of the embankment must be covered with good soil.

18. If there are old streams or traces of landslides in the new embankment foundation, soil holes where tree roots have been removed, and burrow holes and rat holes, they must be filled firmly before adding soil.

19. At ferries and roads, a road slope of 1:15 should be built. If it is a new road, it should not be at right angles to the embankment body. On the river side, it should descend in the same direction as the water flow. On the land side, it should rise in the same direction as the water flow.

20. Bridges must be built or temporary wooden bridges must be built across the new river's transportation arteries to facilitate workers. The supervisor should report to the section office and send personnel to plan in detail and report to the engineering office for approval.

21. When the engineering of each section is completed, the laborers should be ordered to repair and tidy up the new river bottom, bank slope, embankment top, and embankment slope to avoid the disadvantages of uneven height and width.

22. If there are any omissions in these detailed rules, the section office should refer to the actual situation and report to the engineering office for approval and handling.

Shen Bao National Goods Weekly

Words of Contribution

New Thoughts on National Products 205

— Yang An

Chinese people should use Chinese goods. Mr. He Yingqin, during his visit to the Mei Ya Silk Weaving Factory and the Ya Pu Er Electrical Appliance Factory a few days ago, immediately inscribed the eight characters "Chinese people should use Chinese goods." How straightforward and refreshing these eight characters are! Indeed, as Chinese people, we should naturally use Chinese goods. If one is Chinese but only values using foreign goods, that means forgetting that one is Chinese. No matter what, I always feel that it is shameful and not honorable. Further, Chinese people should make Chinese goods, and Chinese people should sell Chinese goods. Only then can we be worthy of ourselves, worthy of our ancestors, worthy of society, and worthy of the nation. I also hope that Mr. He, upon returning to North China, will promote this situation.

Truly National Products One day, I heard Mr. Lu Zhixue telling a joke. He said: "On Sunday, I went for a walk in the park and saw a future master of China lying in a cradle, babbling. Mr. Lu took a look and saw that the cradle was produced by a national goods company, but the people who came to see it all stood around smiling. Mr. Lu observed carefully and realized that they were all laughing at the large characters on the cradle. The cradle was engraved with four large characters: 'Truly National Products.'" Ah, "Truly National Products," these four characters seem very humorous, but they are very touching.

The Chairman is a Regular Customer Chairman Lin Zichao of the National Government, with his youthful appearance and beautiful beard, is approachable. The other day, he made a special trip to the China National Goods Company to visit and purchase national products. For a time, the onlookers were shoulder to shoulder, all wanting to catch a glimpse of the Chairman's demeanor. Later, after meeting with Manager Fang Yexian, Li Kangnian, and Sales Director Shen Jinghui, it was learned that Chairman Lin only visits Shanghai occasionally, but whenever he does, he always visits the company. The Chairman is a regular customer of the company. When the Chairman promotes national goods and loves to use them, it helps to change the atmosphere and influence customs. This is very effective and cannot be compared to ordinary ribbon-cutting and joining in the fun.

The Characteristics of Hunan People My friend, Mr. Lu, attended the Changsha China National Goods Company and returned to Shanghai to describe the development of the Changsha National Goods Company. He said that on the opening day, women from all over the city came to buy goods. The shop assistants were overwhelmed, and even the chairman of the board, Director Tan Qian, and Manager Huo, personally came out to make transactions. Several other stores selling national goods also did an extra one or two thousand yuan in business that day. The people of Hunan are very strong and have a lot of integrity. They are most opposed to unscrupulous merchants and those who sell enemy goods. It is said that they have killed several shameless merchants. Therefore, the establishment of a national goods company is naturally welcomed by everyone.

Suggestions for National Products

Suggestions for a Mobile Exhibition of National Products 206

— A Laborer from Southern China

—Yin salt is not far away, other mountains can be used to grind it—

According to a recent Warsaw dispatch: Poland will soon send an exhibition ship carrying the country's industrial and agricultural products to various countries in the Far East for a practical and effective mobile exhibition. The planned route of this exhibition ship and the Eastern commercial ports to be publicly exhibited are: Port Said, Penang, Swettenham, Singapore, Hong Kong, Shanghai, Dalian, Yokohama, etc.

Poland is one of the countries that revived after the European War, and it seems to have no commercial position in the Far East. Among the imported goods we usually use, we rarely see "Made in Warsaw" or "Made in Poland." Their shipping industry has not yet shown its strength in the Far East. However, in order to promote the sale of their country's industrial and agricultural products in overseas markets, they do not hesitate to invest and specially send commercial ships to the Far East for practical mobile advertising.

This makes me feel that it is not enough for our national goods industry to simply shout and exhibit behind closed doors. There are seven or eight million overseas Chinese in the Nanyang Islands alone, who welcome the arrival of genuine national goods. The chambers of commerce in various ports in Nanyang often want to hold large-scale national goods exhibitions, but they suffer from a lack of contact with domestic national goods merchants. It is also very troublesome to send valuable national goods back and forth. If there are too few goods or they are too ordinary, the scale of the exhibition will be small, and it will not be enough to display the true image of a vast land with abundant resources. The results obtained will naturally not be great.

In the winter of the nineteenth year [of the Republic], I passed through Manila. At that time, the Chinese businessmen in the Philippines were holding a national goods exhibition through the YMCA. They had prepared for four or five months beforehand and spent a lot of effort collecting goods. On that day, in addition to a large group of overseas Chinese, there were many Western couples and wealthy indigenous Filipinos who came to visit the exhibition. It is a pity that there were not many goods on display.

At that time, I thought that if large-scale national goods exhibitions could be held everywhere in the Nanyang ports, it would definitely be of great benefit to the outward development of national goods. However, it is not easy to completely rely on local overseas Chinese merchants to do this.

At present, domestic national goods merchants already have commercially rationalized organizations for production and sales cooperation. If we could take a lesson from Poland and specially transport and ship national goods to Nanyang, Manila, Saigon, Singapore, Penang, Yangon, Deli Medan, Batavia, Surabaya, Sandakan, and other places, circumnavigating for a large-scale mobile exhibition, I think it would be ten thousand times more practical and effective than simply declaring a national goods year.

Talking about National Products

General Mobilization for Promoting National Products 207

— Rong Yu

The National Goods Year of last year has passed, and the Women's National Goods Year of this year is about to end. What have been the achievements of the past two years? I can't bear to say it, but I dare not say it, because the customs statistics clearly tell us that in the past nine months of this year, imports have exceeded exports by more than 250 million silver dollars!

Is it because the promotion has not been vigorous enough? I don't think so. Because the industrial and commercial sectors have been running around shouting themselves hoarse: the intellectuals have been verbally criticizing and writing articles until their tongues and lips are worn out: and there are even some people with lofty ideals who have used bombs as warnings, resulting in imprisonment. There is no lack of such people. Planting such a cause and obtaining such a result is truly disheartening!

Lamenting is useless, we still have to struggle. In this nine-out-of-ten-deaths situation, we still have to make a final effort for national products. I now have a few concrete methods in mind, I don't know if they will work? I am writing them out to discuss with you:

(1) Promote National Goods Education Elementary school students are the future masters. We believe that most of the general adults who have been deeply poisoned by foreign goods are beyond salvation. All our hopes are placed on these young citizens. However, they are like a blank piece of cloth, which becomes blue when dyed blue and yellow when dyed yellow. If we do not train them strictly at this time, they will become foreign goods fanatics in the future. Therefore, in addition to promoting virtue, we should include the use of national goods as an item in daily standard life. If they get used to it when they are young, they will not change their minds when they grow up. Ten years of teaching may yield unexpected effects and harvests.

(2) Those in power should lead by example The government issues brilliant instructions to promote national goods. However, if those in power cannot lead by example, these instructions are as good as nothing. If a major official in a locality can say it and do it, and uses national goods himself, gradually extending it to his subordinates and officials, would the common people dare not follow suit? During the tenth year of the Republic [1921], Feng Yuxiang was the military governor of Henan. He liked frugality and wore a cloth robe and ate hard food. He led by example, and in a few months, no one could find anyone wearing silk in Kaifeng. Using this as an example, as long as those in power promote and implement it, there is no fear of failure.

(3) People Organize National Goods Ten-Person Groups Many people always buy foreign goods secretly. Their conscience is not completely dead, and they always feel a little ashamed. At this time, as long as someone dissuades them, they will naturally not buy them. We are now voluntarily organizing a national goods ten-person group to persuade people to join. Each group is made up of ten people, who supervise and encourage each other. If one person violates the rules, the others will report it. First, there will be persuasion, then punishment, and if they still do not listen, they will be expelled from the group. Everyone has a sense of shame. If everyone else is using national goods at this time and they refuse to use them, wouldn't they regret it so much that they would have no place to hide! From one group to ten groups to a hundred to a thousand to ten thousand, if all the people in the country become members, will foreign goods still have a foothold in our country!

Regarding the above three items, I hope that the officials in the government and the well-known figures in the education sector will promote them first; and all sectors will respond afterward. If we gather the strength of the people of the whole country and launch a general mobilization to promote national goods, the country may have a few hopes of becoming rich and strong!

New News from the National Goods Industry in a Week

(1) Our country's leather goods exports have increased sharply this year, reaching more than 23 million yuan in the first half of the year, surpassing silk and tea to become the first.

(2) Chairman Lin visited the Shanghai China National Goods Company on October 28th, and Minister of Military and Political Affairs He Yingqin visited the Ya Pu Er, Mei Ya, Kang Yuan and other factories.

Beware of Cheap Used Books 208

— Jiang Yun

Recently, cheap used books have often been sold on the market, such as "Dream of the Red Chamber," "Romance of the Three Kingdoms," "Water Margin," "The Family Letters of Zeng Wenzhenggong," "Notes from the Thatched Cottage of Close Observations," etc. The books are printed on newsprint, bound in Western style, with modern punctuation, printed very clearly, and bound very beautifully. The price is very cheap, the cheapest I have ever seen. Most are sold at 10% of the original price, at most 20% or 30%. The complete "Dream of the Red Chamber" used to cost at least one dollar to buy, but now it can be bought for 20 cents. At first, I thought this was the result of the recession, and it was no different from the big sales in ordinary bookstores, but there are so many of these cheap used books on the market that it is shocking. The sidewalks in front of Western-style houses and buildings are often covered with these cheap used books for sale, and I can't help but feel a little suspicious. It wasn't until yesterday that I saw a Guangzhou special report in the Hong Kong Industrial and Commercial Daily sent from Hong Kong that I suddenly realized. This special report is like this:

Two Kinds of Inferior Goods Dumped in Guangzhou Recently 209

Fresh Fruits and Cheap Books

Since the September 18th Incident, after the fall of the northeastern provinces, all Chinese people have been filled with righteous indignation! However, it has only been a short time, and there is no place in the country where enemy goods are not being dumped, almost everywhere we look, causing foreigners to often laugh at our people for their five-minute enthusiasm, which is truly lamentable. Recently, it has been found that the enemy goods being dumped that have newly occupied the market position in Guangzhou are, first, fresh fruits from Taiwan, with Kinzan oranges, apples, and dragon tooth bananas being the most numerous. These kinds of fruits belong to enemy goods and were rarely seen in this city before, but this year they are being dumped in particular, and the number is also considerable. The second is cheap books. These books are completely printed on inferior foreign paper. It is said that after the inferior paper was unsalable, the enemy colluded with unscrupulous merchants to reprint all of our old books and novels that were not copyrighted, and sold them cheaply at 10% or 20% of the original price. Therefore, these inferior paper books are selling very well, and the number is also alarming.

So there is such a dark secret!

Chinese old books have no copyright, so the Japanese use the method of reprinting old books to promote their unsalable paper. No wonder they are selling so cheaply, they are only trying to recover the cost of the paper!

Their methods are truly both clever and vicious! We know that they will print the trademarks of Chinese national goods on their products to sell to Chinese people. They not only manufacture goods used by the middle class and above in our country, but also manufacture goods used by the peasants in the countryside (such as the coarse blue and white bowls used by the peasants for eating, which are also manufactured by Japan and sold to China). Now they are playing this new trick again!

Foreigners' cunning minds are all-pervasive, how should we step up and build our defenses!

National Products and Dance Halls 210

— Dao Qin

The cry of rural bankruptcy is rampant, and the construction of urban enjoyment is indeed a distorted development. In Shanghai, the "ten-mile foreign concession," in recent years, singing platforms and dance pavilions have been built in rows, the city is open all night, the temptation of sex is like intoxication, the pursuit of flesh is like leprosy: here, at a glance, men and women, dressed in fancy clothes, the men are in Western suits and leather shoes, their hair is covered in Stancombe hair cream, shining brightly, and sprayed with Four Seven One One perfume, smelling fragrant, purely a bunch of young masters who spend money like dirt: the women have curly hair, high heels, lipstick, rouge, and powder, showing off their Juna-like figures, delicate and charming, fully revealing themselves as charming girls who cherish their youth and sell their charm.

It can be said that all the men and women here, their clothes, food, shelter, and transportation are all tainted with foreign air, and they have adopted European customs. They are purely the main customers and loyal promoters of enemy goods and foreign goods. Asking half of them to promote the use of national goods is simply as unrelated as a horse and an ox!

However, then again, promoting national goods is not something that can be effective in a very short time. If everyone, men and women, abandons all Europeanized clothing and decorations, never wears Western suits and leather shoes, and never puts on hair oil and powder, and everyone is determined to be a pioneer in promoting homespun cloth dancing and promoting frugal dancing, I think if we can shout this out loud, the masses will respond, and the great effect of changing customs and habits will be more than doubled?

Because the fashionable clothing that is popular in the streets, and the cosmetics and perfumes that are widely sold, are mostly used by singers and dancers first, and then imitated by ordinary women who love vanity and fashion. Most of the pursuit of a certain item and the innovation of clothing styles are due to the singers and dancers acting as typical examples. Therefore, promoting national goods must also start from singing platforms and dance pavilions, precisely because we want to use their great magic of changing customs and habits to make a final movement in the Women's National Goods Year.

National Goods Photo Album

A Record of the Display of Goods Grade Specimens at the North Railway Station 211

— Sun Choucheng

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration, in order to promote national goods, organized a goods grade specimen exhibition room at the Shanghai North Railway Station, and the opening ceremony was scheduled to be held on November 1st. Yesterday, invitations were sent to the leaders of various agencies and organizations to attend the ceremony. This is a good news within the Women's National Goods Year. Therefore, Choucheng made a special trip to the North Railway Station to inquire about the progress of the preparations so far from the person in charge. According to him: The railway authorities, because merchants want to purchase local products, but do not know which place produces abundant products, when a certain product matures, how to pack it and transport it to Shanghai, which is the simplest and easiest to promote sales, so they specially sent staff to the railway line to conduct a detailed investigation, where agricultural products are abundant, where industry is developed, where there are many fish, and where there are minerals. The quality and quantity are investigated clearly, and a list is reported back to Shanghai, and then a list of names is issued, and samples are solicited or purchased from various places, and transported to Shanghai one by one, inspected, and classified. According to the output and price, the number of car transportation costs is set up, and tree windows are set up to display various samples and specimens (those with large quality and inconvenient to display samples, models are made according to the original style, and explanations are added), and they are displayed separately. All are marked with labels, detailing the categories of goods, the level of freight, the address of the product, the annual output, the wholesale price of retail, and the place of sale, so that visitors can see at a glance what they want to handle, and go directly to the place of origin to order, and hand it over to the train for transportation, without having to ask east and west, which can avoid procrastination. At present, those that have been received are roughly divided into five categories: one is mineral products, two is agricultural products, three is forest products, four is poultry and livestock, three is handicrafts, and five categories, the most handicrafts, including metal, copper, iron, kiln products, wood, bamboo, rattan, leather, sail, felt, paper, bone, glue, mat various utensils, as well as cotton, wool, silk various textiles. Mechanical railway mining electrical various materials, paint dye various raw materials, children's toys, household items, about twenty-eight kinds of partners, agricultural products is the second, divided into fifteen categories, including grain, fruit, vegetables, flowers, tea, medicine, etc., mineral products is the next, including coal, slate, mud, soil and other seven categories. Forest products and poultry and livestock are the least, one is four categories such as tree seeds, and the other is five categories such as live poultry, fish, shrimp, fur, etc. Twenty glass cabinets have been made, ready to be arranged in order around the inquiry office, for people to visit. In a word, the national goods collected this time contain all the essential elements of life, including clothing, food, housing, and transportation. The quality and beauty are all excellent, which shows that our country has a vast land and abundant resources, and all handicrafts are not inferior to others. Why should we be addicted to foreign goods to learn fashion, so that the rights and interests flow out, and the words are stern, it seems that we deeply hate the annual increase in imports and sigh that those who do not love the country like to buy foreign goods without a heart, and urge us to publicize it as much as possible to wake it up, so we specially mourn it and it is also what the patriotic compatriots who like to use national goods want to hear.

Education News

Common Expression of Students from Various Universities Regarding the Prohibition of Entering Dance Halls 213

Dancing is not allowed by the new life, and young people should strive to practice it.

To reverse the declining trend, it is especially important for social leaders to lead by example.

Since the joint association of various universities and the school authorities resolved to strictly prohibit students from entering dance halls and dancing, Kong Xiangxi and Wang Zhengting, executive members of the Shanghai District Group of the China Christian Faith and National Salvation Ten-Person Country, also sent letters to the Public Concession, the French Concession, the Public Works Bureau, and the university authorities to ban it. A Shanghai reporter specially asked the opinions of student organizations from various universities in this city on this matter. According to Deng Kangxi, chairman of the Student Union of Jiaotong University, Ren Guqun, chairman of the Student Union of Soochow University, Pan Deguang, chairman of the Student Union of Hujiang University, and the spokespersons of the student organizations of Daxia, Fudan, and Jinan Universities, since Chairman Chiang advocated the New Life Movement in Nanchang, the whole country has unanimously believed that only by implementing the New Life can China have a way out, and the students of our universities in Shanghai can especially understand this and unanimously raise the banner to practice it. Therefore, there was the organization of the New Life Promotion Association of Students from Various Universities before, and branch associations were established in various schools to practice it personally, without daring to slack off. As for entering dance halls and dancing with dancers, it was originally listed as a strict prohibition in the New Life outline and is in the list of things to be thoroughly eliminated. However, there are still some people who do not restrain themselves and still set foot in dance halls, which cannot be said to be completely non-existent. Therefore, to those who advocate prohibiting university students from entering dance halls, the students should show deep sympathy from the perspective of promoting the New Life Movement. However, considering that the decline of social customs is not limited to dance halls, and those who are drunk and lustful in dance halls are not limited to universities, therefore, if we want to shift fashion and refresh society, all aspects should bear their respective responsibilities, and it is especially important for social leaders to be able to practice it personally and lead by example, so that the wind will blow and the grass will fall, and we can achieve the effect of universal advocacy and supervision.

(Nanjing, 31st) Since the National Academic Work Consultation Office started registration, 500 people have requested forms. One has already taken a job elsewhere, and there is still one person named Yi, who graduated from a mechanical engineering school in Belgium. The office has introduced both parties to negotiate, so that the employer can get a practical talent and the employee can get a suitable job. However, detailed measures need to be drafted separately.

Guo Renyuan, President of Zhejiang University, Resigns 215

Secretary-General Wang Shiying Temporarily Replaces Him

The Student Union of Zhejiang University telegraphed yesterday that Guo Renyuan, President of Zhejiang University, expelled two fourth-year students from the Physics Department and the Mathematics Department due to cumulative reasons and at the request of a minority, which caused dissatisfaction among all students. Most of the faculty members also sympathized with the students because the punishment was excessive. On the 30th, Guo accepted the students' request and restored the two students' student status, and resigned to the department because he recognized that the school's management principles were wrong, claiming that he would never return to the school. Students are attending classes as usual. Before the new president is appointed, the school affairs will be temporarily replaced by Secretary-General Wang Shiying, Zhejiang University Student Union.
