Changshu Will Issue Education Bonds 218

Clearing Up Years of Backlogged Education Fees

The Changshu County education budget allocates 400,000 yuan annually. However, due to large-scale fictitious income and actual expenditure, there have been significant deficits over the past three years. Furthermore, the director has changed four times, leading to confusion about the exact figures and a lack of clear resolution. Currently, the second session of the local education representative assembly has been established, placing great emphasis on clearing up the backlogged education fees. The assembly has a plan for addressing this issue. On the afternoon of the 30th, the assembly sent representatives Cai Degong and Jiang Gonglu to the county government to petition. County Magistrate Du Huan personally received them. The representatives explained the situation following the chaos of war. The county magistrate expressed deep sympathy, but emphasized that the restructuring plan should be drafted first by the county education bureau, together with the county party headquarters, enthusiastic local figures, education association representatives, and representatives from various schools, to form a committee to clear the backlogged debts. They should start by investigating the amount owed to each school. If cash is insufficient, they will follow the example of Wu County and issue education bonds, using tax collection as collateral, with the county bureau responsible. Magistrate Qu expressed agreement with this plan, promising to implement it as soon as Education Bureau Director Lu Jingmo returns to the county from the province. However, education association representatives requested that it be realized and completed within this month (November). The county magistrate agreed to expedite the process. As for the July expenses falsely reported to the Education Department, he promised to release the funds immediately.

Recent News on the Municipal Elementary School Construction Project in the Central District 226

The school occupies ten mu of land, with a three-story central building and two two-story buildings on either side, with six classrooms capable of accommodating approximately 400 students. Peking University Stipulates Preferential Treatment for Professors 232

Those Serving Continuously for Five Years Will Receive Paid Leave for One Year

Those Studying Academics During Leave Period May Receive Subsidies to Study Abroad

Liu Fu and Bai Dishizhou Given Condolence Money, Investigation and Introduction of Graduates (Special Dispatch from Beiping) Peking University held its first school affairs meeting of the year at 4:00 PM on the 25th at the Second Institute's conference room. Attending as natural members were Jiang Menglin, Zheng Tianzhi, Fan Jichang, Liu Shuqi, Hu Shi, Mao Zhun, Feng Zixun, Rao Yutai, Zeng Zhaolun, Li Siguang, Zhang Jingqian, Wu Xuan Sheng, Chen Shougu, Zhang Yuan, Dai Xiuzan, Zhang Zhonghuan, Zhao Nianpu, and newly elected professor representatives Tao Xisheng, Jiang Zehan, Zhu Wuhua, Chuan Sinian, Ma Xulun, Zheng Dian, Yan Shutang, and others, more than twenty people. Chairman Jiang Menglin and recorder Fan Jichang first reported on the progress of various school affairs in the morning and the school's implementation plan for the year. The following resolutions were then passed:

School Affairs Meeting Resolutions: 1. Draft regulations on sabbatical leave for professors. Resolution: Committee members Yan Shutang, Tao Xisheng, and Rao Yutai were appointed to review the draft, and Committee member Yan (Shutang) will convene a meeting to review it and submit it to the next school affairs meeting for discussion. 2. Measures for comforting the family of deceased Professor Liu Fu, Mr. Ban Nong. Resolution: A year's salary will be issued to express condolences. 3. Whether the deceased Law School professor Li Huailiang and Graduate School assistant Bai Huaizhou can be granted condolences following the precedent set by Mr. Ban Nong. Resolution: Mr. Li Huaigu and Mr. Bai Dishizhou will each be given two months' salary to express condolences. 4. Establishment of a Peking University graduate investigation and introduction group. Resolution: The secretariat will immediately organize and establish the group. 5. Regulations on student aid, request for amendments. Resolution: The amendments were passed. The meeting adjourned around 8:00 PM.

Professor Sabbatical Research: Article 1: These regulations apply to university professors. Article 2: Professors at this university who have served continuously for five full years, and whom the university wishes to rehire, may take a sabbatical leave of one year. They will receive half salary if they also work, or full salary if they do not work. However, after having taken a sabbatical leave once, they must serve continuously for six years before being entitled to another sabbatical leave. Article 3: Professors at this university who wish to conduct research during their sabbatical leave must first submit a specific research plan, which must be approved by the school affairs meeting to enjoy the benefits of the following articles. Article 4: Professors at this university who go to Europe and the United States for research during their sabbatical leave will receive full salary and a travel allowance of US$350 from the university. Article 5: Professors at this university who go to Japan for research during their sabbatical leave will receive full salary. Article 6: Professors who take sabbatical leave to conduct research in Europe, America, or Japan must spend at least ten months abroad. Article 7: Professors who take sabbatical leave to conduct research within China will receive half salary, and their travel and research expenses will be covered by a detailed budget submitted by the researcher and approved by the school affairs meeting, but the total amount may not exceed 1,500 yuan. Article 8: Professors who have enjoyed the rights under Articles 4, 5, or 6 of these regulations must return to the university and serve for at least one year after the sabbatical leave expires. Article 9: If the university has special difficulties in terms of courses or funding, it may, with the approval of the school affairs meeting, request that professors who have reached their sabbatical leave postpone their sabbatical leave for one year. The postponed year shall be included in the next sabbatical leave period. Those who are asked to postpone their sabbatical leave will retain their sabbatical leave rights if they continue to serve at the university, but the postponed period will not be counted in the service period before the next sabbatical leave. Article 11: The number of professors on sabbatical leave each year may not exceed one per department. Article 12: The university's departments may not hire additional professors because of professors on sabbatical leave, but may hire lecturers if necessary. Article 13: Professors hired under special contracts are not entitled to the rights of these regulations. Article 14: The school affairs meeting may amend any matters not covered in these regulations. Article 15: These regulations will be implemented from the 24th academic year.

Cheng Jinguan and Others Initiate Individual Track and Field Competitions 238

Holding Sports Meets Once a Week

The Goal is to Promote Track and Field Skills

Local track and field comrades, in view of the backwardness of our country's track and field achievements, due to the lack of training opportunities throughout the year and stimulated by the recent expedition of the American track and field team to the East, they have decided to initiate individual competitions to increase interest in sports. Currently, Cheng Jinguan, Fu Baolu, and Qian Xing are in the process of initiating a Chinese individual track and field competition promotion. It is heard that the initiators of the association are Cheng, Fu, Qian, Sun Huipu, Su Xiaoru, Gong Wanyu, Zou Shande, Huang Shengbai, Xu Duo, Ruan Weicun, Kang Kongzhao, Zhou Bangzhe, Zhang Jiazhen, and dozens of others. The purpose of the association is completely different from that of ordinary track and field teams. The goal is to test results and not to compete against other teams. The association will first be initiated automatically by the sports community and then invite sports experts from all over Shanghai as sponsors and directors to expand the organization. Anyone can join as a member, aiming to integrate the entire Shanghai sports community into one. It is heard that the association will launch its activities in mid-month, with the first event planned to be a 5,000-meter open road race around the city (running one lap on the Sanlu Yuan Road). The second event is planned to be the Shanghai men's and women's 100-meter championship. Each competition will be divided into groups to ensure that athletes of varying levels do not compete in the same group. The details will be announced as soon as they are finalized. The aim of the association is to promote this competition method nationwide in the shortest possible time.

Spring and Autumn

Little Western Paradise 249

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Four: A Cup of Water Reveals the Difficulty of Seeking Aid, A Diligent Worker Protects the Elderly; A Thousand Gold Can Be Obtained, Cunning Officials Unite in Groups

Cheng Zhiqian looked at his hesitant expression, and it was difficult to answer well, and it was also bad not to answer. He reached into his pocket to explore for a while, pretending to take out a cigarette, and just kept pondering in his heart. In fact, he didn't smoke, but borrowed this opportunity to hesitate, so that he could think of something to say. After a long time, he thought of a sentence and smiled: "I am also a newcomer to Xi'an, and I am not very familiar with the situation here. But I think that there are also many poor people in Xi'an. If there is no man in the family, should finding a husband's family for the girl be considered an outlet? For example, like your sister-in-law, washing clothes for others and selling some strength is also a way to eat, right? You went to Little Western Paradise to find someone for the girl, that's wrong. All the people there are from outside, without roots and without foundation. Marrying the girl to this kind of person only cares about the present, but what will happen in the future?" Cheng Zhiqian felt that what he said was reasonable and logical. But when Aunt Hu heard it, almost every word was a bit harsh. But she had invited the person, so she must not offend him. She could only smile and say: "Mr. Cheng is right, but everyone has their own difficulties." Cheng Zhiqian clearly knew that she was unwilling, but that didn't matter to his own purpose, he just wanted to see the poor people's families. So he stood up and smiled: "Well, I will be staying in Xi'an for a while, and I will help if you need my help in the future. I just want to see what the situation is like in your poor families. Can I take a look at your house?" Aunt Hu thought, this girl, from the front yard to the backyard of Little Western Paradise, and then to the house, I've really let you see enough, do you still want to see? As long as you are willing to see, then it will be easy to handle, so she smiled and said: "We are such a broken family, I'm just afraid you won't want to see it. If you are willing to see it, then you are our savior. Please take a look." As she said that, she pushed the two wooden doors towards the house, which was considered to mean inviting the guest to enter. (54)

A Record of an Old Man Traveling Around the World 250

— Fu

Those who are only past middle age, with blurred vision, gray hair, shaky teeth, and a senile appearance, are not uncommon in the country. Now, looking at an old man who travels around the world, wouldn't it be more感人to see how different the physiques of Chinese and foreigners are? Mr. Jules Brétepond, the old man, is the Paul of today's Macau. When Mr. Qiu was six years old, he had traveled with his family on long trips. Now, at the age of seventy, he is still very interested in traveling. His travels have already reached Penang Island. He is an American from Southern California, and is seventy-six years old. He used to run a stock business, and has been traveling every year since he retired twenty years ago. This leisurely trip is the fifteenth time he has traveled around the world. Although his beard and hair are as silver, his spirit is very strong, and his steps are healthy, and his heart is happy and pleasant, which makes people know it at a glance. It is said that the oldest youth in the world, with the longest and most optimistic journey, must be Mr. Qiu. From this, it can be imagined that he is getting stronger with age. Mr. Shi's trip around the world was on the President Garfield of the Dalai Company. When asked about his travel impressions, he said: "In total, the journey I have traveled is no less than one million miles, and the cost has reached tens of thousands of dollars. I firmly believe that the best way to make people live longer and stay young is to travel. In the future, I will continue to travel, and I will wait until I die. I estimate that the only places I have not been to are Siberia and Iceland, and I expect that in the near future, I will be able to realize my wish and go for a tour. As for the mileage, the total will be more than two million miles. I am seventy-six years old, and I am getting old. But I am confident that my youthful enthusiasm is no less than before, and I like to be with young people, and I can still swim and dance. All of this is given by travel. Only travel can truly make people young and full of vitality, and now everything is progressing smoothly and comfortably, and the cost is half as much as three years ago. I especially hope that people will remember the joy of traveling to enjoy the supreme pleasure of the body and mind."

Examination of Shaved Eyebrows 252

— Shijiu

Eyebrows grow above the eyes, and their function is, firstly, to prevent sweat from the forehead from flowing into the eyes, just like eyelashes; secondly, the eyes must be supported by the eyebrows in order to show their majesty. Therefore, according to the former statement, eyebrows are like guards of the eyes, without them, the eyes will be bullied by the sweat of the forehead; according to the latter statement, eyebrows are like honored guests of the eyes, without them, only the master—eyes—cannot form etiquette.

Since eyebrows help the eyes, we should protect them well. Unexpectedly, modern fashionable women are willing to shave them away. After shaving them, they feel that it's too bare and ugly, so they draw two thin, narrow, slender ones, which look like they are and aren't. Alas! The guards have been withdrawn. Although the honored guests are still there, they exist in name only. It cannot be said that this is not the eyebrow's misfortune.

Examining it in ancient times, the fashion of shaving eyebrows was also popular in the Tang Dynasty. There is a story in the Tang Yulin written by Wang Dang of the Song Dynasty: "During the Changqing period, the women's headdresses in the capital, with gold, green, pearls, jade, hairpins, combs, and swaying ornaments, were all beautiful, and were called 'hundreds of unknowns'. Women removed their eyebrows, and drew three or four horizontal lines of cinnabar and purple above and below their eyes, which was called 'blood halo makeup'." According to the ancient Beijing makeup, like the current Shanghai fashionable makeup, it was the most beautiful, and the most fashionable. As far as eyebrows are concerned, the so-called palace eyebrows are often quoted in ancient people's poems, and the examples are countless. According to Tang Yulin, the love of fashion of women at that time can be seen. Headdresses only seek beauty, and spare no effort to seek it, so it is said that "hundreds of unknowns." As for removing the eyebrows and drawing three or four horizontal lines of cinnabar and purple above and below the eyes, it is probably not very beautiful. The name of the blood halo makeup, weighed with the knowledge of latitude, is even more unclear. In recent times, the eyes of Hua Dan in Qin Opera seem to have thin lines drawn above and below, which may be the legacy of the blood halo makeup of the Tang Dynasty.

"The depth of drawing eyebrows is in fashion." This can prove that people in ancient times regarded eyebrows as an important decoration on the face. But this refers to supplementing the defects of natural eyebrows. Now that the eyebrows have suffered misfortune, if the eyelashes are aware, they should also sigh that the mission they bear is too great.

Talking About Kunshan Duck Noodles 253

— Zhou Zixin

The pressure of life has made me very distant and indifferent to my hometown—Kunshan. My own close home has turned into a foreign land. How painful is such a long separation! In quiet moments, I often reminisce, and my hometown is worth cherishing, but reminiscing is still reminiscing. In fact, the heart and desire are separated, which only adds to the pain.

I remember, at that time, I hadn't left my hometown yet. Every morning, I would stroll to the noodle shop alone and eat as much duck noodles as possible. At that time, I didn't have any special impression.

After being separated from my hometown and listening to people's praise and my own attempts, my previous views have changed. The duck noodles in my hometown are indeed better than the general duck noodles sold in the market. Fresh, glutinous, fat, and cheap are the characteristics. The general praise is probably due to this reason.

Among the duck noodle shops in my hometown, the first to be mentioned is Longshun Pavilion in Xuanhua Lane near the main street. Their noodles are more glutinous and finer than ordinary ones, and their ducks are more tender than ordinary ones. The noodles and the duck only cost twenty-eight copper coins, and you can taste this delicious and delicious duck noodles. Other restaurants in Baihua Street and Banshan Bridge seem to be slightly inferior to Longshun Pavilion.

The Piao Miao Record of Imperial Incense 254

— Written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, Translated by Qin Shouou

After the Empress Dowager's carriage was properly arranged, we had to hurry into the palace to change our status from being attendants accompanying the Empress Dowager on her eastern tour to being guards left behind in the Fengtian Palace, waiting for the Holy Empress Dowager to return – which is really ridiculous – what is referred to here as 'we' does not only refer to us eight female officials, but also includes Emperor Guangxu, Empress Longyu, and Concubine Jin; because their status in relation to the Empress Dowager is generally that of subjects – although we had to enter the palace first, we were not able to enter through the central main gate, and were not allowed to ride in sedan chairs; therefore we all got out of the sedan chairs one after another, and let Emperor Guangxu lead the way, walking into the smaller doorway on the left in single file. As soon as we entered, we saw a very large courtyard, but our welcoming ceremony could not be held in this courtyard; we walked through it and entered a second courtyard of the same size, and then from the second courtyard, we walked to the third courtyard, which was even larger, about twice the size of the previous one. We rested in this courtyard to prepare for the ceremony.

When we came in, we had brought in the original ancient music team in the palace, and the Western music team that Yuan Shikai had lent to the Empress Dowager; but constrained by custom, the Western music team could not of course play in this formal ceremony, so we had to rely on the annoying ancient music team as before.

At this time, in each courtyard and in each palace, there were already many eunuchs distributed to serve. Half of these eunuchs had always been stationed here; most of the rest had been sent by Li Lianying before the Empress Dowager set off to sweep the halls, arrange the flowers and trees, and prepare everything that was needed, so that when the Empress Dowager and we arrived, there would be no shortage of supplies. (164)

Miscellaneous Remarks

About Servants 255

— Lingzhi

Although my family subscribes to the Shenbao, I read the articles in the Chunqiu column every day; however, due to busy work, I don't read every article. Even the "Piao Miao Record of Imperial Incense," which I am very interested in, I sometimes read and sometimes don't. Therefore, I didn't see the description of Yuan Shikai calling himself "servant" when he saw the Empress Dowager, nor did I see the attached note a few days later, saying that someone had sent a letter correcting that Han officials should call themselves "subject" according to the Qing system. However, I did see Mr. Yi Sheng's article, "Servants of the Former Qing Dynasty." Because Mr. Yi Sheng's speech was quite incomplete, and because I happened to have existing materials on hand, I took the opportunity to discuss this issue of titles.

(1) It is an old Manchu custom for Manchu officials to call themselves "servant."

The imperial edict to the Grand Councilors, Qianlong 23rd year, 2nd month, Ren Shen, said: "Manchu ministers...should still call themselves 'servant' in regular memorial reports to request peace and express gratitude, in order to preserve the old Manchu custom."

From this, it can be known that it has always been the Manchu system for Manchu officials to call themselves "servant," and it was not newly established by Hong Chengchou.

(2) Not all Manchu officials call themselves "servant."

The same imperial edict says: "Manchu ministers call themselves 'subject' or 'servant' when reporting matters, and the wording is inconsistent. It is ordered to transmit that subsequent official business memorial reports should be called 'subject,' and regular memorial reports to request peace and express gratitude should still be called 'servant'..."

From this, it can be seen that whether Manchu officials call themselves "subject" or "servant" depends on the nature of the memorial reports, and it is not always the case that they call themselves "servant." However, this only refers to civil officials, not military officials.

(3) When Manchu and Han officials jointly report official business, they use the title of the chief guard as the title.

The imperial edict to the Grand Councilors, Qianlong 35th year, leap May, Ding Wei, says: "Today, Zhou Yuanli, together with Xining, etc., reported on a memorial concerning the search and capture of locust plagues...In the list of names in the memorial, Xining Daling'a called himself 'servant,' while Zhou Yuanli called himself 'subject,' which is quite ridiculous. Subjects and servants are originally one, and are both titles of offering to the superior. Although the meanings of the words are different, the principle is the same. Manchu and Han officials naturally have different titles, but when they encounter ministerial memorial reports, even senior Manchu officials also uniformly call themselves 'subject,' and Manchu governors and governors-general also do so when reporting local official business. It is not that the title of 'servant' is considered humble and close, while the title of 'subject' is considered honorable and distant..." However, the list of titles in the memorial should not be mixed. It should only be based on who is the first title, whether Manchu or Han, and it can be consistent. In this memorial jointly reported by the three people, since Ning's name is listed first and he is called "servant," then Da Ling'a and Zhou Yuanli should write their names directly in succession. Why bother to make distinctions in between?"

However, in another imperial edict, the statement is different.

(4) When Manchu and Han officials jointly report official business, they should uniformly call themselves "subject."

The imperial edict to the Cabinet, Qianlong 38th year, November, Wu Shen, says: "Today, Censor Tianbao and Ma Renlong reported on a memorial concerning the discovery of cheating in the examination of teachers...Because Tianbao was in front in the memorial, they were all called 'servant.' In the past, memorial reports by Manchu officials were generally called 'servant,' and those by Han officials were generally called 'subject.' This is just a continuation of the old practice...It is not that calling oneself 'servant' is close and respectful, while calling oneself 'subject' is distant and discourteous...In the future, all joint reports of official business by Manchu and Han officials, both inside and outside, should uniformly call themselves 'subject,' in order to show unity. It is hereby ordered."

Zhou Yuanli was reprimanded for refusing to follow the Manchus in calling himself "servant," while Ma Renlong was criticized for following the Manchus in calling himself "servant." It can be said that he was caught between a rock and a hard place, and was easily blamed!

(5) There are also Han people who flatter and call themselves "servant."

The imperial edict of Qianlong 38th year, November, Wu Shen, criticized Ma Renlong for calling himself "servant," explaining that he had never discriminated against calling oneself "subject" or "servant," just to prevent ignorant people, or those who flatter and call themselves "servant," and it is necessary to guard against its spread. The imperial edict of Qianlong 35th year, leap May, Ding Mao, also stated that there is no difference between "servant" and "subject," and he never cares about such things. Even if some Han people call themselves "servant" during audiences, there is no intention to reward them. From the sentence "Some Han people call themselves 'servant' during audiences," it can be seen that although Han people do not have to call themselves "servant" as a rule, there are still many Han people who are willing to be servants!

(Note: The above imperial edicts were compiled by Mr. Chen Yuan'an and published in the sixth issue of the Weekly Journal of the Institute of Sinology, Peking University. Readers who wish to see the full text of the imperial edicts can refer to it.)

The only major settlement period of the decade.

Silver and Money Trades Particularly Busy 258

Interbank Lending Rate at Eight Percent... Cashier's Check Premium Greatly Increases

Yesterday was the only major settlement period of the tenth decade. The silver and money trades were at the end of a long-term overall closing period. The busyness of the settlement procedures was, as usual, impossible to escape. All kinds of routine settlements were also more tedious than usual. Therefore, the market situation yesterday was a rare one in each year. The interbank lending rate in the foreign market still opened at six percent in the early morning, but in the noon market, due to the Bank of China receiving over two million in cashier's checks, the market atmosphere suddenly tightened and the interbank lending rate rose by two percent, hence eight percent. The premium on cashier's checks initially opened at 0.08 or 0.09 percent, then reached 0.15 or 0.16 percent. The situation suddenly became tense, and people's hearts were stirred. In the interbank lending note transactions, early morning transfers totaled over 4.1 million, new transactions totaled over 500,000, and there were especially many transactions in the noon market, totaling over 1.2 million. Transactions in the Small General Association totaled over 900,000. The long-term settlement and closing amount for both the silver and money trades totaled over 30 million. Over 2 million in foreign pledges were redeemed, and the amount of new pledges made was as high as nearly 5 million, a huge number. It is said that this session involved over 2 million in housing pledges that had reached the end of their one-year and six-month terms, which is why the amount was particularly high. Bank settlements, due to the excessive number of transactions, could not be checked in detail for the time being and could not be verified. According to rough estimates, foreign banks had over 20 million, Chinese banks had several hundred million, and Japanese banks had approximately 20 million. The number of money shop public bond settlements was too high to estimate in terms of time, but it was approximately 70 to 80 million. The settlement of foreign cashier's checks totaled over 16 million, remittances from various routes totaled over 1.5 million, cash receipts totaled over 1.2 million, banknote receipts totaled over 1.5 million, and banknotes issued totaled over 2.2 million. Customer sources were 300,000, and expenditures were 400,000. Also, the total number of exchanges at the clearing house on the 31st was 17,747,936.51 yuan, including 6,824,798.48 yuan in silver dollars and 10,655,038.03 yuan in silver dollar remittances.

Total Interbank Lending Rate for October 260

The total interbank lending rate for October was 2.17 yuan. Among them, the Double Ten holiday had one day off, which should be added by 0.06 yuan, so the total was 2.23 yuan, with an average daily rate of slightly less than 0.072 yuan for 31 days. According to our calculations, the interbank lending rate in foreign markets was slightly higher at the beginning of the month, constantly above 0.1 yuan, but by the 5th and 6th it had already begun to decline. Subsequently, it stood at 0.06 yuan per day until the end of the month, without any change, resulting in the above total. As such, a deposit rate proposal will be made at tomorrow's general meeting, likely at 2 yuan or 2.5 yuan.

American Bank is Loading Cash Again 261

Our country has always been a net importer of silver, but this year is uniquely different, with large quantities being exported to Europe and America, all by foreign banks. Since the 15th of this month, after the Ministry of Finance ordered customs to implement an increase in the silver export tax, various foreign banks, having no profit to be made, immediately stopped trading. Therefore, silver exports have been virtually nonexistent for half a month. However, there were occasional exports to South China, but not very large. Yesterday evening, the reporter passed by the Bund Wuma Road Public Works Department pier and saw Rongmao Transport cars fully loaded with silver, being unloaded onto iron barges. Upon inquiry, it was said that they were being loaded by an American bank for transport to England, totaling about 200 boxes, estimated to be worth over 1 million yuan.

Flour at 299,000 Bags

Wheat Totaling 33 Cars

Yesterday was the tenth-month flour delivery period, and the total number of deliveries throughout the day was still huge, totaling 299,000 bags. Among them, Fuxin's various factories' Yibing Chuan Wharf receipts totaled 292,000 bags, most of which were new goods, and a small portion were returned goods. Xinda's Yuan Paotai totaled 7000 bags. As for the receiving side, the silver and money gang's hedging totaled around 200,000 bags, and the customer gang and this street received around 80 to 90 thousand bags. The industry insiders were flowing out due to factory receipts, and the quantity was considerable. If actual sales encounter setbacks in the future, there is a risk of decline.

Yesterday was the tenth-month wheat delivery period, with a total of 33 cars. Number 6 delivered 6 cars, Number 23 delivered 13 cars, and Number 26 delivered 11 cars. The receivers were Number 1 receiving 6 cars, Number 6 receiving 13 cars, Number 17 receiving 5 cars, and Number 32 receiving 9 cars. It was heard that the receivers were generally representatives of the factories, with factories such as Huafeng and Xinda receiving around 10 cars each, and the rest being purchased by customer groups.

American Wheat Has Risen Back 273

After the wild drop of the 29th, Chicago wheat rose back today (30th). Brokers were purchasing quite vigorously, and locals were settling more, so there was progress. The market is calm, and there is a current lack of outside participation, so it is predicted that it will not be very strong. The spot market continues to rise, and the difference is even greater. Chicago wheat's closing price on October 29 and closing price on October 30.

River Bottom Rice Market Reverses to Lively 274

(Shanghai South) Yesterday, over twenty shipments arrived from various origins (totaling over three thousand piculs). The initial quality appeared good. However, wholesale buyers became hesitant, with only the Qingdao group purchasing just over two hundred packages of six varieties. Furthermore, buyers were stricter with their quality standards, rejecting anything not considered top-grade, and driving hard bargains, causing some discouragement. Market conditions suffered a slight setback, but by closing, the market tightened somewhat. The price of new, thin rice like the six varieties improved by several points, while the market for thick, new short-grain rice such as Wild White remained stable. Due to limited supply of imported rice, “Du Yang Jian” brand saw prices increase. Other varieties such as “Bian Yin Yuan” showed no significant change.

(Shanghai North) Yesterday, about twenty boats of various goods arrived from the river bottom region. Sales of various rice types in the market: New short-grain, broken short-grain, aged white, “Yuan Yin,” new “Yang Du Jian” saw sluggish wholesale movement. Kiln-dried new and aged "Bu Ke Jian" were relatively active. The market for high-quality new short-grain rice increased by 10-20 cents; medium to low-quality increased by 20-40 cents. Broken short-grain increased by 20 cents. Aged white and "Yuan Yin" increased by 10 cents. Top-quality "Du Jian" increased by 20-30 cents, and mid-to-low quality increased by 10-20 cents. Densely planted new "Yang Jian" and new and aged "Bu Ke Jian" also increased in price.

Locally Grown Indica Rice and Coarse Rice Continue to Rise by 20 Cents 275

A Total of Fourteen Thousand Packages Sold Inland

Future Imported Rice Sees New Transactions at Higher Price of 9 Cents

Yesterday, local Indica rice sold very well, and market sentiment was particularly good. While arrivals were continuous, with 4,000 packages from Hunan and Hubei, new shipments from Yueqing, Jiangbei, and Wuhu were limited. All arrivals were snapped up by local buyers. Yesterday, 2,500 packages of Hunan machine-milled rice and 600 packages of Wuhu Indica rice were actively sold in this district. Inland demand was very good. Wuxi buyers were present at the market, competing for purchases. A total of 1,000 packages of Hunan broken and aged rice, 4,500 packages of Hansha coarse rice, and 850 packages of Jiangbei and Yueqing rice were sold. Due to competition among buyers, coarse rice jumped more than 20 cents, and machine-milled rice rose nearly 20 cents. However, Guangdong rice saw no transactions due to suspicion of being mixed with imported rice.

The market for imported rice remained strong. Yesterday, 3,500 packages of Saigon spot rice were sold. Inland buyers took 500 packages each of broken and future imported rice. Prices should have risen, but after the arrival of 50,000 packages from Saigon, importers refused to lower prices. As a result, the price only increased by 3-5 cents. However, speculators held onto future imported rice, expecting higher prices. Yesterday, a British merchant, Jinlong, released 500 tons of March Saigon rice, which was purchased by Yuanfeng at a price of $5.19, 9 cents higher than the previous market price.

Oilseed Cake Market Sees General Increase 276

Recently, sales of soybean oil cake have been quite active. The reason is that prices are low and sales are brisk, and prices in producing areas are also reported to be rising, so sellers are mostly holding tight. Yesterday, 14-15 carts of new and aged soybeans were traded in the market, with prices rising by 4-5 cents to 6-7 cents. There were inquiries for bean cake from Wenzhou, Shantou, and other places. Seeing the tightness in the market, traders in this district also started buying, with over 20,000 pieces traded in the overall market. Prices rose by 2 cents in both the morning and afternoon. Soybean oil and peanut oil also continued to rise by 20-30 cents, with 500 pieces of peanut oil and 200 pieces of factory oil traded. A total of 1,500 pieces of Dalian, Niuzhuang, and Qishan oil were traded.

Sugar Market: “Five Blessings” White and Rock Sugar Sold as Soon as They Arrive 277

Yesterday, the sugar market was characterized by firm customs gold, which, while logically indicating tightness, sales remained sluggish, and the trend remained difficult to reverse. The guild set prices for #24 coarse granulated white sugar at $18.80 for spot goods and $18.90 for goods from this store, but there were no transactions at the original prices. Higher-grade #8 and #9 Dutch brown sugar was priced at $14.20, while lower-grade ordinary goods were at $14.05, gradually loosening. Goods for re-export were at $5.10 but were not yet being marked out. Only 100 bags of re-export #24 coarse granulated white sugar were traded at $5.55, a decrease of 5 cents from the previous day. This factory’s cotton white also decreased by 10 cents. #1 Zhenyu ice was at $17.20, and #2 was at $17. The factory’s #1 rock sugar was at $22.90, and #2 rock sugar was at $22.70. The 200 boxes of "Five Blessings" white ice sugar that arrived the day before were reportedly sold out as soon as they arrived, at a price of $17.80 per slab. Future arrivals are temporarily scarce, and market sentiment is very stable.

Dried Goods: Tong'an and Anhai Longan Expected to Open Today 278

The Anhai and Tong'an dried longan that arrived around the middle of this month, totaling about a thousand pieces, were being held by the buyers due to their high cost, in anticipation of a better market. However, sales have not been very brisk recently, and it has been difficult to raise prices. They have been held until now without opening. It is now reported that the guilds from both sides will meet today to jointly evaluate the goods and discuss prices. If they agree, sales will commence. Otherwise, they must telegraph the owners for their consent before a transaction can be made.

Metal: Tinplate Merchants Hoarding 279

The recent arrival of tinplate is not much, and inventories are running low. Moreover, telegrams from overseas report skyrocketing prices. As a result, traders of this commodity are thinking of manipulating the market. The standard market price is rising incessantly, now estimated at $16 (90-pound single-sheet German goods), $17 (90-pound single-sheet American goods), $31.50 (90-pound double-sheet German goods), and $33 (90-pound double-sheet American goods). Both 100-pound single- and double-sheets are up by $1. Transactions are exceptionally strong among manufacturers, and wholesale buyers are also active, so the trend is to corner the market. Moreover, those in the trade with ample capital are also finding ways to hoard, resulting in even less circulating stock, and the market is expected to continue to soar.

Free Talk

On "Don Quixote" and Similar Works 280

— Jia Zhifang

I heard that someone is about to start translating the complete works of Gorky. This news, at first hearing, is quite astonishing.

Chinese translators, in the past, were mostly peddlers. Although some have rolled up their sleeves to tackle the complete works of a certain foreign author, judging from the few volumes published, some parts were translated so badly that they lost all resemblance to the original. Several major works of Turgenev (not the complete works, of course) have been translated, and some seem to have two versions. Good or bad aside, they were completed. Tolstoy, a name known to anyone with a bit of literary sense, but until now, his "War and Peace" still doesn't have a complete translation! Gogol's "The Inspector General" has been translated, but his greatest work, "Dead Souls," hasn't had the chance to shake hands with these square characters! No wonder Mr. Xu Xia, the translator of "The Nose," said that more civilized countries have translations of it. The youth who are eager for translations complain about this piecemeal policy of the translation world, even more than Mr. Xu Xia.

That’s the first point.

More ludicrous is that some foreign masterpieces have only had their names introduced. Among them, Cervantes' "Don Quixote," though frequently cited by domestic writers in their articles, like a household name like Ah Shi, the book, it seems, still hasn't been translated.

Our translation world once had a flood, but in recent years, translations have been rare, almost silent. However, it is said that the translation world is about to revive. Magazines alone, "Translation" is foremost, followed by "World Literature," which is naturally a welcome phenomenon.

I remember an article I had with Mr. Gu Zhongyi in literature, "My Opinion on Translation." The gist of Mr. Gu's opinion is that those engaged in translation should have an overall plan for translation. Now someone translating the complete works of Gorky and the like can be considered a satisfactory answer.

I also have an opinion, but unlike Mr. Gu's overall plan, it is very small. I only hope that translators can translate some works that have been quoted by writers in their works. This is called "paying back the debt," because our authors guide young people to learn by telling them to buy a book like a history of literature in the market, check the representative works of each school and representative author in it to read; some only say in a general way, learn from foreign authors; some pick up a pen and endlessly open a minimum reading list of literature books. However, in a word, the use of each school, each author, each representative work mentioned in the literature history in the market, or the minimum reading list opened, to some learning youth, at most is a demonstration once, there is nothing else.

In modern China, eight or nine out of ten literary youths are not very wealthy. They read some foreign books as difficult as eating swan meat. This refers to those who can speak a foreign language. As for young people who are not from school and have no chance to learn a foreign language but still want to engage in literature, such as shop clerks and workers, when they hear the author's talk or thesis that they must learn from foreign authors but cannot get the translated works of the author, isn't this a basin of cold water pouring on their heads, determining that they have no literary qualifications?

The talk is far away. We are clamoring for a large number of reserve writers, but we do not give them food to eat, or give a little bit of leftovers, snacks, etc., soldiers still have to mutiny, and those who learn literature do not seem to be so wild, but it is inevitable that they will change careers halfway, even if they keep their chastity to the end, and the works they produce are yellow and thin, malnourished!

This is the future crisis, as long as we do not admit that literature is absolutely something that some special people play with in an ivory tower.

Translators may have an overall plan to do it, or choose to start, but don't be like the Shakespeare complete works translation association in Peiping, which has been hanging up for several years, just wish and not repay. Not only that, in addition to repaying the wish, we also want to ask domestic translators to temporarily stop issuing empty checks!

Tokyo Correspondence (Part Two) 281

— Zhang Xiangshan

Before entering prison recently, Mr. Lin once said some arrogant words: He called himself a person who turns to persuasion, a guide to repentance, compared to the mentor of Kobayashi Takiji when he overcame opportunism.

At the same time, in the realm of pure art, voices of abuse arose. He cursed the shamelessness and lack of conscience of the converted writers, even comparing them to bandits (magazine) chaos. This righteous indignation indeed attracted attention. However, on the reverse side, Nakamura Takao, who was cursing people as turncoats, himself came from the art school to the path of popular literature (please note that Japanese popular literature is different from Chinese popular literature, Japanese popular literature is the Zhang Henshui style of China). Wen Yuan's dream of pure art, along with his to be completed great work "Life," all stopped together. Not only him, but even Mr. Kikuchi Kan, who attacked Maeda Kōichirō's artistic politics with great arrogance, is also wandering in the garden of popular art.

The conversion of the former, needless to say, is entirely due to the adverse objective environment, which also makes the subjective conditions adverse. The latter's conversion, however, is due to the inevitable material desires of the capitalist era. The manuscript fees for writing popular literature, such as Eiji Yoshikawa, Miki Mikazuki, etc., are around two or three thousand yen per month, while pure art writers probably only get a few tens of yen per month, how far apart! This material temptation inevitably pulls writers who are immersed in urban life into the valley. The poet Saijō Yaso once said, I write a pure art poem at most give me about 30 yuan, if I write a popular song for the gramophone stage, it will be more than a few hundred. For life, I have to write popular songs. This kind of extremely great material temptation is so terrible.

In short, the conversion problem occupies a considerable dispute in today's literary world. They mutually recognize each other, but do not reflect on themselves, and there is no deep thought of re-departure after the conversion, and in the end the problem is more and more chaotic.

The present is indeed the season for revival and popularity. After the disappearance of the voices of classical revival, literary revival, etc., the subjective revival has followed.

Kawabata Yasunari, a leading writer of the pure art school, has recently lamented the weakness of the subjective, the new writer Yadan Qi discusses the improvement of the subjective, and Lin Fangxiong also sings the emphasis on the subjective. The season of the subjective revival has indeed come to the Japanese literary world.

In a time when human life is about to be extinguished under the heavy pressure of the objective, it is certainly not unreasonable to introduce this kind of argument. Under the inability to break the objective heavy pressure, this is the inevitable natural cry, but the problem is how to take the reason of this subjective. For example, Mushanokōji Saneatsu's writing of subjective, is indeed speechless, but in the end, what kind of emphasis and take the reason, to deal with the subjective? The thing that attacks Mushanokōji Saneatsu's subjective is positivism, that is, its objectivity and scientificity, which is indeed a victory in literature. The subjective that we advocate now must be built on the soil of victory. In this way, there is the progressiveness of the subjective. If not, it can produce the ghost of Mushanokōji Saneatsu. This point is indeed the thing that must be paid attention to when Japan is advocating the subjective revival.

Recently, the work that became the problem in the literary world is "Is it a God or a Woman" by Muroo Saisei (Literary Arts, October). This article describes a man who has four concubines and manipulates four women very well. In fact, this thing does not have great advantages, it can only describe the different psychological states of each, and the success of the psychological analysis of the male protagonist Kamahara, but the shortcomings of this article are quite a lot, first. The protagonist is written as someone who has money, and it is of course needless to say that he can buy the hearts and bodies of women with money, and the four people on the other side do not have a strong horse. Furthermore, the male master's need for many women should of course be to suit himself, to yearn for the noble beauty, and to conquer the opposite sex, but in reality, he is written as the man's lust, in the disease and goodness, there is an unintentional decadence of existence. However, although there are the above shortcomings, but in the current time when the works of the pure art school are not prosperous, it is indeed easy to move the attention of all the critics in Japan in October, because there is that sharp psychological analysis.

Finally, let's talk about an interesting incident. Recently, a certain magazine asked various writers about their second choice, that is, what would they like to be if they did not become literary writers. The most interesting answer was that of Ozaki Shirō, who said: If you allow me to be unreasonable, then perhaps I would be a thief, a pickpocket. Others, such as Rin Tarō Takeda's bourgeois or imperial soldier, Kojiro Serizawa's judicial officer, close to Akai, Wulin Dream Hall, Zhang Xiazhou and other politicians, heroes; new graders painter, etc., are all answered very interestingly.

Autumn in the North 282

— Lin Xi

Autumn in the north is like a sad erhu.

The erhu is really not something to be loved. Have you ever seen an erhu solo in a concert? As big as a piano, as small as a harmonica, they can all make the dark audience breathe with the rise and fall of the melody; but the erhu's noisy melody has never been loved by the general public. But imagine, if you are in the deserted outside the Great Wall, your heart is as empty as the emptiness of the earth, you want to cry, but you don't know what makes you cry; looking far away, the sand is connected to the sand, the wind is blowing the sand, and the sand is also sending the wind; the sky is too empty, also too lonely, there is one thing less on the earth, and there is one thing less in your heart; this thing is like the incense in front of the mourning hall, like the red cover on the coffin, which can absorb the tears from the bottom of your heart. I say, this thing is the sad erhu. It is like a steel needle, yes, it is a steel needle, stabbing the sky, stabbing the earth, and also stabbing your empty heart. The sound is alive, undulating, it is sad and mournful. The sound is like crying, but not purely sad crying, it is like a hero of the world, in the time of frustration and proof, even if it is helpless, he wants to find a way out of helplessness. Su Wu in the ice and snow probably tasted this taste, but Su Wu still has his flock of sheep to chat with him for comfort. If it is a general of the border, trapped outside the foreign land, in that realm, it is no wonder that he will shed tears. Autumn in the north, will make people feel like this.

Autumn in the north is like a border poem.

Border poems are rich in exoticism, this exoticism contains a sad component, but not the sadness of "bright moon rises from the sea, we share this time of year"; the Tao sadness is magnificent, belongs to the "great wind rises, clouds fly, where can we find brave men to guard the four directions", it is the sigh of "the energy pulls the mountain, the strength covers the world and sighs what to do", it is the "Yi River bank, the autumn wind is bleak. A brave man, waves and crosses". "The wind and dust of the Han Dynasty make the sun dark, and the red flag is half rolled out of the camp door," like these words, does not give you the impression of the Han Dynasty indifferently? In the desert of the border, the wind rolls the dust of the clothes, layer upon layer expanding in the dim sunlight, looking over it is so translucent, like behind thousands of troops, raising a cloud of dust, from the dust faintly you can see the back of the army and horses: and the dim sunlight, shining on the turbid dust and mist, makes the realm more dim and sinking: in the dimness, the more you look at the empty wilderness, this brings some empty taste. Filling this emptiness is also just the empty wind, dust, and dim sunlight, this is really helpless emptiness: this can make people look at the wilderness and very much want to exhale hard. Autumn in the north will give people such a mood.

In the south, it is difficult to have autumn, but that is lingering, like a moonlit night, like a song: it will make people think of the childhood clothes box, in the clothes box is the childhood mother's clothes; compared, the same is autumn, and their distance is just like the north and south in geography. When the grass turns yellow in the south, the autumn plains in the north are already sending dust with the dim sunlight.

Lonely Person 283

— Feng Mu

Lonely flowers bloomed in the heart of a lonely person. In a very lonely place, I lonely remember:

One very clear morning, the provincial stadium began the rare hustle and bustle of the past: on each row of grandstand benches, accumulated thick dust, people automatically wiped it. That is to say, the crowding of people has not made people care about the opportunity. This was the day after the opening of the provincial sports meeting two years ago, my friend Pan Jun was the selector of the 1500-meter event of this sports meeting. He was only fourteen years old at that time, but he was selected in our school and won the right to participate in this competition.

Naturally, with his age and physical strength, the result was failure, but he reached the end and ran fifth without taking. In the end, he had an unusual record in the newspaper the next day: he was praised as the white-robed young general among the thirty-six heroes.

Like this place! I clearly and intimately remember.

Two years later, I ran to this place again today, and the situation of this place is not different from now: so crowded people, so crowded place, so crowded situation, so crowded... but my friend, died of pneumonia this summer!

Saying that, I was sad. I missed my friend's glorious fragment, and my tears could not help but fall.

"Right here! Right here!"

Saying that, I, this lonely person, ran out again with a gray-white heart.

"Seeds of sorrow!"

This shout was brought down from the tears.

Bells 284

— TK

Dou Fang (Seven) 285

— Wei He

What are you writing!

But I didn't answer him, just gave him a fierce look, and quickly and hastily wrote down. Every time I wrote a word, he would look for it in the book, sometimes he thought he was dazzled and couldn't see it. So he pointed his finger to find it, and asked those gentlemen to see, but they all said it was different from the book. And he also saw that I suddenly wrote so fast and so hastily, it seemed that I was deliberately wasting paper, asking him to lose money, which really surprised and angered him to the point of turning pale.

What exactly are you going to write?

Seeing that I had finished writing "behind vermillion gates, meat and wine stink", and then wanted to write "on the road, corpses of the frozen lie," he couldn't help but get angry.

Who told you, who told you to write like this, beast! He slapped the table and scolded: Does this count as a couplet?

He pulled my ears and hit my head on the table, breaking my nose, and the blood flowed all over the golden and brilliant ten thousand years of red, seeping open piece by piece.

Father was originally weak, but that time when he hit me, he seemed to have a lot of strength, every hit was very effective, so that I couldn't hide it even if I wanted to. Mother came to persuade, but it was useless, as if I had committed a heinous crime, and he looked so brutal that he treated me like an animal.

You want to scrape my face, don't you? You want to collapse my stage, don't you? You beast, I will whip you to death, whip you to death...

I seemed to be spinning in a whirlwind, and I felt pain in all directions. My eyeballs seemed to explode out of my sockets, and I was dark for a while, but then I saw countless sparks stirring. My head was buzzing, and my mind was confused and I couldn't tell the faces of people.

What's wrong, Dad?

I was worthy of myself struggling in pain, just repeating this sentence. The original anger and shame had already formed a lump at that time, like fatigue, pressing heavily on my heart.

Father disregarded everything, just gritted his teeth and hit, sometimes shouting beast, don't you say more. Helpless mother, was also crying next to him. As for those adults and gentlemen, some didn't say a word, standing aside to watch; some pretended to say a few sarcastic remarks, polite and polite; some quietly slipped away; and even more were particularly cheerful to help the old man scold me:

It's reasonable to hit, children are so disobedient, according to their own wishful thinking, hum, it will be terrible in the future! (End)
